(Tokyo) According to the telegram received by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs from Tanaka, the consul in Petropavlovsk on the 15th, the Soviet court in Petropavlovsk on the 14th began hearing the appeals of the arrested fishing vessels Haikoku Maru, Hamayoshi Maru, Kotohira Maru, Dairyu Maru, etc. The Japanese side presented a list of powerful material evidence and argued for innocence, but the Soviet side did not recognize it and rejected the appeal. Therefore, the Japanese side attached some material evidence and requested a postponement of the hearing, but the Russian side still did not recognize it and rejected it in one fell swoop. All cases of drifting near territorial waters due to force majeure were determined to be acts of illegal fishing in violation of territorial waters, and the harsh measures taken in the previous trial against the Japanese ships were deemed valid. (Washington) Former US Navy Major Farnsworth, accused of selling naval secrets to Japan, pleaded not guilty at his trial this afternoon. Farnsworth was arrested this morning. His subpoena stated that the defendant gave a secret publication entitled "US Naval Intelligence Affairs and Security" to a certain Japanese naval officer. Authorities claim that the officer's name is now known and hinted that he could be captured soon. After being arrested, Farnsworth told people that he had not sold US naval secrets to any foreign country. He also said that he had talked with a representative of "a certain Oriental government" about the possibility of organizing an air force abroad, but he did not know whether this representative was Japanese or Chinese. He did not know any classified documents, but said that some documents about naval affairs had been stolen from his home. As for the nine Midwestern states today, the sun is still scorching, and there is no space left in the hospitals. The highest temperature was said to be 112 degrees in Carbon Dale, Illinois. However, in places where it has rained, the temperature is below 60 degrees. The cool air blowing in from the Pacific Ocean through North and South Dakota is too late for the crops, but it has relieved the suffering of people and animals, and after the temperature drops, corn may still be revived. Travelogue of Japan (2) 79

— Our reporter Hu Zhongchi, Hu Yizang

As we entered Nagasaki Port, the sights on the shore caught our eye. The most striking was the Nagasaki Shipyard, which leaned against the mountain. Long shipbuilding platforms made of interlaced steel bones stretched out into the sea, with several hulls under construction alongside. Our ship passed by there and docked at the pier. We were going to Kobe, and since the ship had a four-hour stop in Nagasaki, we went ashore. We took a rickshaw to our consulate. As we rounded a corner, we saw the blue sky and white sun flag of the consulate waving in the distance. The consulate was near the Shusshi Bridge, a two-story Western-style building with a small yard in front planted with a few trees and plants. An elderly Japanese maid in the guardhouse at the door handed our business cards in, and we met Consul Liu Ruxiang and Secretary Guo Jianying in the reception room. Consul Liu was from Guangdong and had been working in Nagasaki for many years. We could see his forthright personality from the expression in his conversation. He had a harmonious relationship with the local administrative officials in Nagasaki. The local government originally wanted to implement a law to increase taxes on Chinese traders, but it was temporarily shelved because of his efforts. We talked about the Japanese news industry. According to him, the major Japanese newspapers could only speak for the military and the government and could not be considered representatives of public opinion. The Fukuoka Nichinichi Shimbun in Kyushu was comparatively more outspoken and often had sharp criticisms of the military and government policies. He also said that Japanese newspapers often contained many inaccuracies about the internal affairs of China. When he met Japanese journalists who came to visit, he often criticized them to their faces for their lack of understanding of China. Consul Guo was proficient in painting and had often contributed to our newspaper a few years ago. At that time, he asked about the recent situation of friends in Shanghai. We talked with Mr. Liu and Mr. Guo for a long time, and when other guests came in, we said goodbye and agreed to visit again when we returned from our trip.

We left the consulate and strolled around the street for a while before returning to the ship. The scenery was excellent as the ship headed towards Kobe. The islands of various sizes that came into view were all lush green. We passed by those islands the next morning as we passed through the Seto Inland Sea. Most of this sea area is forest, and occasionally, we could see well-organized agricultural fields.

At 2:00 PM, the "Nagasaki Maru" docked in Kobe, almost twenty-four hours after departing from Nagasaki. We handed our luggage over to the Japan Travel Bureau, and we ourselves carried our hand luggage ashore and walked a long way before reaching customs. The customs officers turned every one of our large and small boxes inside out and asked about the value of some of the items inside before writing the letters "OK" on the outside of the boxes in pink chalk. The strict customs barrier was finally passed. Only then did we feel relieved.

Two Entering the Gateway to Western Japan

Leaving the customs, we saw the green peaks of the Rokko Mountains in the distance. We especially noticed the two circular marks formed by the green forest on Mount Suwa, one was the city emblem of Kobe. The other was an anchor pattern, presumably symbolizing this great world harbor with international ships coming and going. We took a "Taxi" (cars waiting for hire on the street) in front of the customs to a pre-arranged inn. The minimum rental fee for a "Taxi" was 50 sen, and the fee increased according to mileage after the trip exceeded a certain distance. We passed through several wide and well-organized city streets, glimpsed many magnificent buildings, and felt that the city of Kobe, known as the gateway to western Japan, was very comparable to our Shanghai in terms of construction.

The inn where we stayed was not far from Sannomiya Station and was a purely Japanese-style building. Although the facade was not large, the internal facilities were very complete, and the layout was very refined. We stayed in a room upstairs by the window. The interior decoration was full of artistic interest. The patterns of the window frames and the styles of the paper doors were different on each side, but they were very harmonious. The room was filled with a simple mood. Neither the floor nor the wooden pillars were painted. On the wall hung a "Celestial Maiden Painting" with Nandina and daffodils. Below it was an elegant potted plant. Opposite the window was a plaque with the inscription "The Taste of Tea and the Taste of Zen." The calligraphy was very refined, and it was signed "Jizaian." All of this arrangement made us deeply feel the Japanese people's universal artistic taste and charm.

Nagasaki Shipyard

The Sale of the Tianjin Huaxin Yarn Factory: Difficult to Operate Due to Pressure from Japanese Yarn Factories; All Six Beiyang Yarn Factories are Nearing the End 80

Tianjin Correspondence: The Tianjin Huaxin Spinning Factory held a shareholders' meeting on the 13th. The opinions of the shareholders included the following: (1) The machinery is old, consumes a lot, and produces little. There is a lack of large funds for renovation; (2) The current situation in North China is unstable, and the Japanese textile industry is advancing into Tianjin, using its large capitalist system to control the North China economy. The shareholders have no courage to invest huge sums again to increase capital; (3) Banks are reluctant to lend money due to the unstable situation; (4) Foreign debts have been repeatedly extended, but the creditors are pressing too hard and must be paid off immediately. Based on the above four reasons, everyone agreed that it would be better to sell out rather than continue operating. If there are those willing to take over and are willing to pay a reasonable price, then the share capital can still recover 20% to 30%. After deliberation, it was decided to appoint directors Liu Junqing and Xu Jishang as responsible persons to contact outside parties for the sale. Before the sale, no matter how difficult, they will still try to maintain operations to avoid the severance of livelihood for the majority of workers. The original text of the shareholders' proposal for the sale at this meeting is recorded as follows: "Respectfully, our factory has been operating poorly for years, and shareholders have no profits to share. Although this is due to the economic downturn, human efforts have also not been perfect. We have heard that there was a slight surplus last year, but no actual profit. If this continues, the shareholders will be asking for the moon. Recently, the situation in North China has become increasingly urgent, with endless changes. In terms of politics and economy, ×× is using every means of pressure. Several of Tianjin's large yarn factories have already changed hands. Our factory, at this time of great change, does not know what good strategies can be expected to overcome this difficult situation. If we continue to procrastinate and do not revitalize ourselves, I am afraid that we will also go bankrupt in a few years and become the achievements of other factories. It is better to plan early, either to close the factory or to sell it out, so that the shareholders' capital will not be completely lost and there will be no hope. We request that your committee quickly determine the major policy direction and make plans to prevent future troubles. (The following is omitted)."

The Huaxin Yarn Factory is the smallest of the six major Beiyang yarn factories, with 27,000 spindles, 15,000 in the Tianjin factory and 12,000 in the Tangshan branch. Its operations are well-managed and its management is quite innovative, so in recent years, although the North China industrial sector has been shaken by crises, this factory alone has been able to stand firm. However, since this year, smuggling has been rampant, and the sales of smuggled yarn have become more widespread. In the past, every bale of yarn sold incurred a loss of about 10 yuan, but now it has increased to more than 20 yuan. The sales routes in southern Hebei and western Shandong have all been taken away. Although Huaxin is well-managed, it still loses two to three thousand yuan a day. Recently, the Japanese Toyo Textile Company is building the Yufeng Yarn Factory Tianjin factory (the main factory is in Shanghai) in Tianjin's Special District Four. Construction has begun and will be completed in April next year and the factory will open in October. The first phase is 50,000 spindles and 1,000 looms, and the second and third phases are planned to have 100,000 spindles. The Yuyuan Yarn Factory was sold to the Japanese Zhong Spinning Company and renamed Public Great Sixth Factory, with 75,000 spindles. Although the machinery is old, it will be renovated. The Yuda Yarn Factory, managed by Japanese merchants, originally had 30,000 spindles and is also planning to expand and purchase new machinery. Huaxin, looking around at its situation, has no ability to compete and fears that after the yarn factory is completed in one year, there will be no need to resist and Huaxin will have to close down. At that time, even if it wants to sell out, it will not be possible, so it is better to plan early, hence the previous resolution. It is rumored that the buyer has been determined to be the Greater Japan Textile Company. If the deal is completed, then three of the six Beiyang factories will fall into Japanese hands, one factory will be closed (Baocheng), and He Hengyuan and Beiyang will be managed by a trust company organized by the banking community, almost like the light of a dying ember. (14th)

Hebei Province Handles General Village Clearance: Joint Defense and Suppression of Bandits on the Border between Hebei-Shandong and Hebei-Henan; Implementing the Baojia System and Conducting Household Registration 81

Baoding Correspondence: In order to eliminate bandit troubles in the province and consolidate local security, the Hebei Provincial Government previously divided the entire province into ten security zones, each with a bandit suppression commander responsible for bandit suppression and drug prohibition matters within its jurisdiction. It was also permitted to divide the stationed troops into four regions: southern Hebei, western Hebei, central Hebei, and northern Hebei, to jointly suppress the remaining bandits in each region. Therefore, the major bandit disasters in various parts of the province have been successively eliminated. As for sporadic small gangs, they have also largely gradually disappeared. However, the southern Hebei area is adjacent to northern Henan and western Shandong, and the mountains in the Wuan and Shexian areas of northern Henan are connected, making it a bandit's nest. In addition, the bandits take advantage of the limited defense zones of the stationed troops on the provincial border to travel back and forth, causing harm for years. Governor Song Zheyuan of Hebei Province is now determined to eliminate these roaming bandits and has specially implemented joint defense with the Henan and Shandong authorities. Regarding the joint defense issue in the Hebei-Henan border area, the Hebei border is jointly undertaken by the Chen Huafu Brigade of the stationed troops, and the Henan border is undertaken by the Huang Guanghua Division of the stationed troops. When necessary, both sides can also cross the border to pursue and attack. Therefore, the border areas of the two provinces are currently very peaceful. The joint defense measures between Hebei and Shandong are handled by Song Zheyuan and Shandong Governor Han Fuju in person. The defense zone is near the Tianjin-Pukou Railway, including Dezhou in Shandong and Qinghe, Wuqiao, Qingyun, and Gucheng in Hebei. In the past, large gangs of roaming bandits often occurred, but now there have been no major bandit disasters. From now on, the source of bandits in Hebei Province will be cut off, and local security can be guaranteed.

In order to eliminate bad elements in various counties, the Hebei Provincial Government decided to start by strengthening the basic organization of the people, so it organized the baojia system and conducted household registration. The provincial government stipulated detailed measures and ordered all counties to implement them. The organizational steps are to establish one jia for every ten households, with a jiazhang (jia leader), one bao for every ten jia, with a baozhang (bao leader), and one zongbao (chief bao) for each township, with a zongbaozhang (chief bao leader). The method of jia organization is to start from one side of each village or town and conduct household registration door-to-door. If there are not enough households for one jia, a jia can be established for six or more households, and five or fewer households can be merged into the neighboring jia. This work has already begun and is scheduled to be completed by the end of August. All able-bodied men aged 18 to 45 in various places must be listed in a separate register. The first step is to train the bao leaders and jia leaders, and then the bao leaders and jia leaders will train the able-bodied men, so that the local able-bodied men can have the power to defend the local area themselves. Currently, blockhouses have been built in various counties, and the baojia organization will also be completed. There will be no place for bad elements to stand. (July 11)

The Water Level of the Lower Yellow River Rises Sharply: Lisheng Village Has Risen a Total of Five Meters in Four Days; The Yellow River Estuary Project Will be Completed Quickly 82

Jinan Correspondence: Since the major flood last year, the people of Jiangsu and Shandong provinces have suffered deeply. Whenever they hear of the Yellow River rising, they rush to tell each other, showing a great fear of tigers. Now, it is not yet the flood season, but flood warnings have been repeatedly issued, and the increase in river water in recent days has been unprecedented. According to calculations by the River Affairs Bureau, the upstream Lisheng Village in Shandong Province rose more than four meters from the 10th to the evening of the 12th, and another nine inches and seven points from the morning of the 12th to the morning of the 13th, for a total increase of about five meters in four days. The main current is surging unusually. The upstream of Shandong Province has many dangerous works. The various cofferdams are severely impacted by the water. The Director of the River Affairs Bureau, Han Fuju, telegraphed various general sub-sections to strictly guard against this, so all the officers and soldiers along the river have been paying attention and preparing for emergencies. Although the river water is high, the works are still stable. At Kang Village upstream, the water level dropped six inches on the evening of the 13th. The main current impacted the tenth to twentieth cofferdams and side-injected the fiftieth cofferdam. Also, Wang Jinfu, the acting county magistrate of Zhencheng, telegraphed on the 12th that the river water was rising, and the main current was moving back and forth between the cofferdams, and that he was supervising the workers to add pressure, and the situation was still stable. The diversion canal dug opposite Kang Village was largely completed, and the current has been released into the canal on the morning of the 12th. The River Affairs Bureau has already telegraphed the provincial government to report this.

Kong Xiangrong, Chairman of the Yellow River Conservancy Commission, came to Jinan on the 10th of this month and then went to the downstream of Lijin to inspect the Luanjingzi Caiwan project. On the morning of the 11th, he went to the construction site with Deputy Chief Engineers Zhu Yong and Pan Yifen in the rain. At 6:00 PM on the 13th, he arrived at the construction site and inspected the first diversion canal of the Luanjingzi water diversion dam and the Shunguang Weizi water diversion dam and the second diversion canal. Currently, the diversion canal project has been largely completed and is being expanded to make the water discharge easier to flow smoothly. The dam construction is also progressing day and night and will be completed soon. Kong gave detailed guidance on each item of the dam construction and diversion canal project and urged the dam construction to be completed as soon as possible, so it was agreed to add 1,000 workers, add a night shift, and continue to purchase wooden piles and straw materials for defense. From the current observation of the river's current and shape, everything is very good. Once the water level is slightly higher, the water-blocking riverhead and river tail left at both ends can be opened to allow the water to flow straight down. Not only is it convenient for shipping, but the water discharge is also smooth. The completion of the reorganization of the estuary can be called a partial success. After Kong completed his inspection, he returned west with Deputy Chief Engineer Zhu and others and arrived in Jinan at 9:00 PM on the 13th. He took the Shanghai-Ping train that night to Beijing to attend the water conservancy conference. Once the conference is over, he will still return to Shandong to inspect the downstream project and inspect and guide flood prevention along the river. (13th)

The Case of the Murder of the Manager of the Jinan Japanese Shinhwa Company is Solved: After the Four Criminals Were Arrested, the Mastermind Xu Gongyang Was Executed by Shooting; Li Xuezeng and Others Sentenced to Imprisonment 83

Jinan Correspondence: Ando Heisaburo, the manager of the Jinan Japanese Shinhwa Company, was hacked to death with an axe by drug dealers Xu Gongyang, Si Rongxuan, Xie Fenggang, Li Xuezeng, and Wang Xingzhu on the night of the 23rd of last month, and four bags of heroin were robbed. They then fled one after another. After the case was reported, Shandong Governor Han Fuju immediately offered a reward of 2,000 yuan for the arrest of the fleeing criminals and ordered the military police to solve the case within ten days. The Liu Yaoting Department of the Third Road Special Detective Team and the Fourth Section of the Public Security Bureau successively arrested Xu Gongyang, who carried the axe to commit the crime, and accomplices Si Rongxuan, Li Xuezeng, and Xie Fenggang in Yucheng, Jinan, and other places. Only Wang Xingzhu was at large. They were escorted to the Public Security Bureau and then transferred to the Military Law Department of the General Headquarters for interrogation. This case has now been adjudicated. In addition to executing the principal offender Xu Gongyang by shooting, the remaining accomplices Li Xuezeng and the other three were sentenced to fifteen years of imprisonment. On the 13th, the Military Law Department of the General Headquarters escorted Li Xuezeng and the other three to the court for execution.

The Ripple Effect of the Wuxi Silk Workers' Strike: Female Workers March and Clash, Instigators Arrested, All Factories in the County Remain on Strike 84

Wuxi Correspondence: A work slowdown arose among the female silk factory workers of this county. After the party and government organs convened a meeting to mediate, they set a deadline of the 15th for all factory workers to return to work. It is now known that on that day, some of the more compliant workers had already gone to work. However, a portion of the female workers, about six or seven hundred, did not enter the factories to work when it was time to start. Instead, they set off on a march, heading to the Yongtai Silk Factory on Zhizu Bridge in the South Gate, intending to cause a disturbance. They were stopped by the police officers of the Public Security Bureau's Third Precinct, security team members, patrol units of the Public Security Bureau's Inspection Office, and river patrol units, leading to a clash and great disorder. A temporary curfew was declared in the area near the factory. The female workers then went from Yangyao Bay to Guangfu Gate, intending to petition the General Labor Union. Upon reaching Guangfu Gate, they were again stopped by police, who forbade them from entering the city to prevent any accidents. The city gates were closed. At the same time, female workers in the Eastern Gate area also clashed with the police, and the Eastern Gate was also closed. Later, the entire police force dispersed the female workers, averting a major disaster. After about half an hour, the city gates were reopened. Another group of workers gathered at the Silk Factory Industry Labor Union, demanding relief. They were also driven out by the security brigade's Second Squad. The various precincts increased the number of guards at each city gate to maintain order. The county government, concerned about the expanding strike, issued a strict prohibition. At the same time, it ordered the Chief of Political Police, Wu Zhengrong, to lead political police Xie Xiaodi and other Public Security Bureau officers to arrest Gao Dehua, a suspect in instigating the strike, in Zhou Shanbang, and Lu Liangqing in Wanqian Road. Ge Xinde, an inspector of the Public Security Bureau, also arrested Xu Tangshi. All were taken to the county government. In the afternoon at 4:00 PM, Section Chief Li Duxuan held a court hearing and ordered them to be transferred to the Second District Commissioner's Office for further investigation. The representatives of the Silk Factory Industry Labor Union, Ye Qiaoyun and others, numbering over ten, believed that this strike was instigated by a Land Commissioner from the county party headquarters, so they turned him over to the county government for disposal. The Second District Commissioner's Office ordered the county government to strictly arrest the ringleaders and to enforce a resumption of work within a specified period. However, the workers insisted that they could only resume work after the party and government resolved the conditions they had put forth. Therefore, all the silk factories in the county remained on strike.

Hu Boyuan Discusses the Scientification of Economic Construction 85

Hu Boyuan, a technical expert at the Ministry of Industries, a mining and metallurgy specialist, and a prolific author, gave a lecture at the Nanjing Central Broadcasting Station on the 10th, titled "The Scientification of the National Economic Construction Movement." The following is a summary of the main points: "Today, as a representative of the China Scientific Movement Association, I am here to broadcast. I chose this topic, but it is very broad. Due to time constraints, I cannot go into detail. I intend to focus on the important points of the National Economic Construction Movement and promote them using scientific methods. This is just a small contribution of my opinion. I hope the listeners will correct any omissions or inaccuracies. If a country wants to exist on this earth, it must have a goal, rally its people, and lead the entire nation together onto the ideal path. This ideal path is the one that suits the country's environmental needs. For example, before the European War, the Germans aimed to dominate the world by force. After the Meiji Restoration, the Japanese aimed to compete for hegemony in East Asia. The Americans aimed to maintain the Monroe Doctrine. The British aimed to hold the reins of world commerce. Although their goals were different, they were all striving for self-preservation. The one thing they had in common was that they wanted the whole country to work together to achieve this goal and continue to maintain it. Today, the most dangerous thing for China is economic bankruptcy. The way to save the country is not to resist the enemy, but to focus on economic construction. Therefore, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, seeing this, launched the National Economic Construction Movement, a head-on blow, like a bright light in a dark sea, setting this as the goal for the entire nation. It is the only effective remedy for revival in this day and age. However, having good goals and good talents, it is necessary to have good methods to use and promote them in order to see results. What are these methods? They are to promote them based on scientific principles. This is the actual topic I will talk about today. The slogan of the Scientific Movement Association is to use scientific methods to organize our country's inherent culture, to use scientific knowledge to enrich our country's current society, and to use the scientific spirit to create our country's future life. It is also said that scientific socialization and social scientification, in other words, use known scientific knowledge and methods to organize or create all past and future undertakings in society. For example, both Japan and Russia use scientific methods to build everything, rather than relying solely on scientific inventions to do construction work. There are two main points in our country's economic construction: (1) To enable the nation to be self-sufficient in common daily necessities such as rice, wheat, cotton, steel, and oil, in order to reduce imports. (2) To increase the export volume of our country's unique products such as furs, tung oil, silk, tea, soybeans, nickel, antimony, and tin, in order to balance imports. There are two principles: one is to develop basic industries and transportation construction, which should be promoted by the state or organizations, and the other is to promote agricultural production and small-scale industries, which should be promoted by the people. There are two steps: one is to have existing talents go deep into the people, cooperate and cooperate, publicize and guide, to correct long-standing habits, and the other is to cultivate talents to continue the movement in an ordinary and orderly manner. Because our country's economic construction is different from that of Soviet Russia. Soviet Russia has a foundation for its industry, and its people are accustomed to scientific training. Therefore, its construction plans can be successful in years. The knowledge of our people is superficial, and they lack organization. Therefore, starting economic construction cannot be done quickly, but must be done with steady and arduous means. Here are a few examples to illustrate how to promote our country's economic work using scientific methods. Hu then described in detail the steps and methods of the four construction movements of agriculture, industry, mining, and transportation, citing various statistics as proof of the facts. Finally, he said that the scientific movement should pay attention to the following four key points in order to achieve the goal of economic construction. The so-called four essentials are (1) regarding finance, (2) regarding organization, (3) regarding talent, and (4) regarding laws and regulations. Hu's segmented discussion was extremely detailed.

Wujiang: Request to Build a Station Canopy 86

Wang Zuxun, chairman of the local Chamber of Commerce, stated that the Sujia Railway is scheduled to begin passenger train service on July 15th. However, the Wujiang station's platform canopy and over-track overpass have not yet been built. If passengers encounter rain while boarding, they will have nowhere to take shelter. Moreover, crossing the tracks to the opposite platform is extremely dangerous. Yesterday, he specifically telegraphed the directors of the Two Railways Bureau, Director Huang, requesting that the Engineering Department be promptly ordered to plan and construct them as soon as possible to benefit travelers.

Suzhou: Concubine Murdered by Paramour 87

On the morning of the 14th, a nude female corpse, with brick wounds and signs of strangulation, was discovered in a rice field in the Youcheqiao area of Sukun Road outside Qimen in Suzhou. Next to the corpse was a seven- or eight-year-old girl, seriously injured but not yet dead. That day, the court conducted an autopsy and sent the injured child to the Gospel Hospital for treatment. After this case occurred, it caused a sensation throughout Suzhou. The Public Security Bureau also immediately sent detectives to investigate the perpetrator. It is now known that the deceased, Ms. Xia, was 34 years old and the wife of Ji Zhongyuan, a rickshaw businessman at No. 63 Lindun Road in the city. Ji is 34 years old, from Qingjiang, and used to live in Qiaosikong Alley. He earned a decent living by renting out rickshaws. He married Ms. Xia in 1925. The injured girl, named Gendi, is nine years old and Ms. Xia's daughter. The family of three lived happily together. Ji had two friends, Yin Amao and Chen Asheng from Chuansha, who jointly opened the Chen Senji Construction Factory in Dongyue Temple in Zhenjiang. Amao had recently become involved with Ms. Xia. On the 11th of this month, Amao came to Ji's home from Zhenjiang, claiming that the construction factory he had established had contracted to build houses near Sukun Road and was willing to pay Ji a monthly salary of 18 yuan to hire him as an accountant. Ji did not agree. That night, Amao stayed at Ji's home. The next day (the 12th), Ms. Xia and her daughter Gendi claimed to be going out to buy groceries, but they disappeared with Amao at the same time. When Ms. Xia left, she was wearing a dark silk cheongsam. As for the reason for the murder, it is suspected that although Ms. Xia left with Amao, she regretted betraying her husband and quarreled with him, leading to her death. The deceased's body has been autopsied and claimed by Ji for burial. The Public Security Bureau is currently sending out detectives to investigate the perpetrator, Yin Amao.

Dinghai: Setting Up a Shortwave Radio Station 88

The Dinghai County Government, in order to facilitate communication with the various islands, plans to establish shortwave radio stations in Zhoushan, Daishan, Qushan, Putuo, Liuheng, Jintang, and other places. It submitted a request to the Provincial Government's Department of Civil Affairs and Department of Construction for approval. However, the original plan was to use five 5-watt shortwave transmitters. The order was changed to use a 5-watt shortwave transceiver and a three-tube shortwave receiver. As for the management personnel, two specialized technicians have been hired, and five police officers have been selected for training. The total start-up cost is more than 2,500 yuan. The equipment will be purchased and transported by a construction company. The five police officers are currently being actively trained so that they can start communicating as soon as the equipment is installed.

Zhenjiang: A Section of the New Canal Completed Surveying 89

The largest water conservancy project in Jiangsu Province this year is the opening of the new canal in the coastal reclamation area. Several months have passed since the entire staff of the surveying team set out to survey. Although it is now hot weather, the surveying work is still actively underway. The Department of Construction previously reported that the 150 kilometers from the He Duo River to the Zhan Huang River have now been surveyed and is currently engaged in design and drawing to determine the basis for implementation. The remaining sections will continue to be surveyed in order to complete the project as scheduled. The Department of Construction is carefully planning this project, and it has not yet been determined whether a separate agency will be established to handle it in the future.

Flood Prevention Begins Along the Yangtze River 90

The Department of Construction has separately ordered the seven counties along the Yangtze River—Zhenjiang, Jurong, Jiangning, Jiangdu, Yizheng, Jiangpu, and Luhe—to plan for flood prevention and to appoint responsible flood prevention personnel to be in charge of their affairs in order to avoid negligence. Recently, the seven counties including Zhenjiang have respectively appointed commissioners to start flood prevention and have reported it to the Department of Construction for record.

Yangzhou: Fisherman Catches Giant Century-Old Turtle 91

The Daokou River outside the West Gate of Yangzhou connects to the outer river. The river is wide and deep, and fishermen regard it as a habitat. Many people fish with nets and hooks. Yesterday (the 13th), a fisherman named Zhang Changyi caught a turtle in that location. Its shell was as black as iron, and its four feet had white hair. It weighed more than eighty pounds. Old fishermen said it was a century-old creature. It was purchased by an elderly man for five yuan, who said he intended to send it to the Shanghai Zoo for feeding. According to Zhang Yumen, a medical researcher, the glue made from this turtle can be taken to prolong life.

Aftermath of Gathering to Protect the Dike 92

Farmers in the Gualuzhou Balipu to Yangziqiao area of the second district of Jiangdu gathered to protect the dike. On the 16th, they detained more than twenty tugboats from various companies going upstream and downstream. Finally, at 6:00 PM, they reached an agreement to release the towlines and let them go. It is now known that since yesterday (the 13th), the Fourth District Department of Water Police sent Captain Dai, along with the Shipping Association, the Transportation Bureau, and representatives from the various shipping bureaus, together with local people and the local township chiefs, to negotiate with the dike-protecting people on two traffic solutions: (1) Within the scope stipulated by the Transportation Bureau's water level, each upper and lower wheel will be towed alongside the slow lane. (2) If the water level exceeds the scope stipulated by the Transportation Bureau, the upstream wheels will dock at the Fourth District Department's door, the downstream wheels will dock at Yangziqiao, and the tugs will be pulled to the docking place to exchange tows to avoid the risk of flushing the dike.

Nantong: Changes in the Fourth District Security Organization 93

The organization of the Fourth District Security Command has been ordered to change. Commissioner Ge serves concurrently as the commander. The original Chief of Staff, Peng Longxiang, has been changed to Deputy Commander. After the county magistrates concurrently serve as the chiefs of the security brigades of the counties under the jurisdiction of Nantong, the brigade adjutants of the counties will be transferred to each other. He Keqian of Haimen arrived in Nantong on the 14th to take over as the adjutant of the 16th Brigade.

Salt Merchants in Nantong Seek Relief 94

Salt merchants in Nantong are seeking relief from the Transportation Department because they have too much salt in storage, resulting in insufficient economic turnover. It has been decided to pledge the stored salt to the bank for a loan of 3.5 jiao per bag of salt, with a total pledge amount of 3 million yuan.

Gaoyou: Rice Prices Gradually Rise 95

Recently, rice mills have been raising rice prices step by step due to the limited amount of rice stored during this time when the old crop is running out and the new crop is not yet harvested, coupled with the hot weather, which makes it difficult to ship goods. Each shi has increased by 8 jiao and will continue to increase. On the 12th, glutinous rice was 13.2 yuan per shi, dwarf xian snow tip was 12.6 yuan, red shell tip rice was 11.8 yuan, and red brown rice was 11 yuan.

Ningbo: Notorious Bandit Zhou Xiaosheng Executed by Firing Squad 96

Zhou Xiaosheng, a notorious bandit from Xiangshan West Township, entrenched himself in the Bajiao Hengshan area, engaging in kidnapping for ransom, murder, and arson, committing numerous crimes. Previously, the Ningbo Public Security Bureau's Detective Team arrested him in Shanghai and transferred him back to the original county. The Xiang County Government, upon orders, took the bandit to the West Teaching Ground at 7:00 AM on the 12th and executed him by firing squad. Onlookers were numerous and applauded.

Yaochang People's Salt Barn Established 97

Since the Three North Housen Salt Barn in Yuyao Dongxiang was closed last year, the Yaochang people have accumulated salt and have been unable to sell it, which has cut off their livelihoods. As a result, they repeatedly requested the Yaochang Administration to establish a people's salt barn. Later, the Yaochang Transportation Department approved the establishment of the Yaochang Left Salt Chang, which is now established and scheduled to begin collecting and releasing salt on the 15th. Rong Wanqing will serve as the Barn Director.

True Cholera Discovered 98

Recently, the weather has been sultry, and true cholera has been discovered. Yesterday, Ye Ashun, a cook at the Gongdelin Restaurant on the north bank of Jiangbei, suddenly turned pale and his whole body was covered in cold sweat like rain while he was working at 11:00 AM. He suddenly fainted and lost consciousness. After being sent to the hospital for diagnosis, it was learned that he had true cholera. Despite receiving a cardiac stimulant and saline injections, he could not be saved and died instantly. It only took half an hour from the time he fell ill to his death. The Department of Health has instructed citizens to take precautions quickly. In addition to paying attention to diet, everyone should receive preventive injections.

Bengbu: Large Batch of Suspect Sugar Seized 99

The smuggling of private sugar to the south for dumping has recently continued unabated. Although there have been repeated seizures here, unscrupulous merchants are still selling it secretly. The Bengbu Public Security Bureau recently received a tip that the Rintai, Yongfeng, and Xiehe sugar and paper stores on Jingyi Road in this city had private sugar hidden and were selling it secretly. They dispatched long-term police officers to investigate on the 13th. They found 183 bags of Dong sugar and 184 bags of Taigu sugar in Rintai, 50 bags of Dong sugar and 425 bags of Taigu sugar in Yongfeng, and 303 bags of Dong sugar and 319 bags of Taigu sugar in Xiehe. However, the store owners of the three sugar and paper stores firmly denied that it was private sugar. For the sake of caution, the Public Security Bureau extracted a portion of the seized sugar and sent it to the Bengbu Inspection Office of the Customs for forwarding to Nanjing for testing. All the sugar seized was sealed in the respective stores and will not be moved temporarily. It will be verified after the examination and identification.

Crackdown on Geisha's Unconventional Clothing 100

After the public prostitutes here were renamed geishas, regardless of whether they were from the Suzhou, Yangzhou, Qing, or Huai gangs, there was no longer a name for prostitutes. Recently, the New Transport Promotion Association believed that most of the geishas in the city were wearing strange and unconventional clothing, which was a great loss of simplicity, and that some were wearing white hats and short skirts, imitating the dress of female students, and should be cracked down on. A method of correction was specifically discussed, and the Public Security Bureau was requested to order geishas' clothing to be simple, with red trim on the clothes for identification, and to prohibit dressing up as female students in order to maintain customs. After approving the letter, the Public Security Bureau often ordered the sub-bureaus to notify all the geishas in the city to comply with the shares and not to disobey. Upon hearing the news, the geishas believed that the red trim on their clothes was a matter of face and mostly adopted a wait-and-see attitude and refused to comply. The general pimps held a meeting at noon on the 12th to discuss how to deal with the situation. They decided to comply with the order not to allow geishas to wear white hats or dress up as female students, but they would appeal to the Public Security Bureau regarding the red trim on their clothes, which was a matter of face, and request that the order be withdrawn. They also felt that the geishas' monthly donation of 10 yuan was too heavy and planned to request the authorities to reduce it appropriately in order to alleviate their hardships. It is said that the Public Security Bureau is determined to implement the crackdown on geisha clothing, otherwise, it will not count even if all the geishas go on strike.

Guangdong Customs Tax Supervisor Not Nominated, News from Bank of China Headquarters 103

Regarding the issue of Chen Jitang sending personnel to the Guangzhou Branch of the Bank of China on the 14th to forcefully withdraw customs tax deposits, a reporter from the Central News Agency interviewed Song Ziwen, chairman of the bank, yesterday morning. Song said that he had been away from Shanghai for many days and had just arrived in Shanghai, and was busy with affairs, so he sent someone to meet him on his behalf. It is said that the annual customs tax revenue of the Guangdong Customs Office is 17 to 18 million yuan, all of which is deposited in the Guangzhou Branch of the Bank of China. Smuggling in North China has been rampant for the past six months, and the Guangdong Customs Office's tax revenue has naturally decreased. The current deposit in the Guangzhou Branch is as high as 8 to 9 million yuan. Unexpectedly, Chen Jitang sent personnel to the bank on the 14th, strongly requesting to withdraw it. The branch authorities refused, arguing that Chen's actions did not comply with the bank's business regulations, and reported it to Shanghai by telegram, stating that Chen's strong desire to withdraw the customs tax was not only related to the national treasury, but also to foreign debt guarantees, which was also of great importance. For the sake of performing its duties, the bank is determined to do its best to protect it. As of noon on the 15th, Chen had not yet seized it. All branches of the Bank of China in Guangdong Province are still operating normally. It is also known that the exchange rate between Shanghai and Guangdong silver dollars is 600 yuan, which is another 10 yuan lower than yesterday.

After the Shanghai Labor-Capital Mediation Committee resolved the case of citywide silk factory workers demanding the restoration of their previous wages, workers at all factories uniformly resumed work yesterday morning. Sujia Railway Opened to Traffic Yesterday; Director Huang Accompanied the Train to Jiaxing; Reception for All Sectors at the Yanyu Tower 108

Construction of the Sujia Railway began in February of last year. Due to the numerous rivers and streams and the many bridges and culverts along the line, it took a year to complete. Yesterday, it was officially opened to traffic. Jin Shixuan, a representative of the Ministry of Railways, and Huang Boqiao, director of both railway bureaus, accompanied the train to inspect the entire line, and hosted various sectors from Shanghai, Suzhou, and Jiaxing to tour the Yanyu Tower in Nanhu Lake and report on the construction process. The line is temporarily operating four round trips daily. In the future, the number of trips will be appropriately increased based on business conditions. The details of the opening are recorded as follows:

Special Train Departure

Those from Shanghai who participated in the opening ceremony included Fan Shouzhi, secretary-general of the railway bureau; Xiao Weiguo, chief of the transportation department; Wang Zhigang, deputy chief of the transportation department; Cao Xinzhi, deputy chief of the general affairs department; Wang Bi, chief of the mechanical department; Wu Naixian, chief of the police department; Wu Xihan, chief of the documentation section; and over twenty people including reporters from the Central News Agency. They departed from the North Station at 4:45 AM yesterday morning on a specially prepared train to Suzhou, arriving at Suzhou at 6:40 AM. There, they met with Huang Boqiao, director of both railway bureaus, Zhou Wuyi, special commissioner of the Ministry of Railways, who had arrived in Suzhou the previous day, and dozens of reporters from Suzhou newspapers. At 7:20 AM, they were attached to the first passenger train from Suzhou to Jiaxing. There were no particular ceremonies at the opening, only the national flag of the Kuomintang was affixed to the head of the train, and the band of the Wuxian Public Safety Bureau accompanied the train, playing music. It was very simple.

Scenery Along the Way

The Sujia Railway is 74.44 kilometers long and has 99 bridges and culverts. The construction cost was approximately 3 million yuan. There are eight stations: Wuxian (Suzhou), Xiangmen, Wujiang, Bachai, Pingwang, Shengze, Wangjiangjing, and Jiaxing. Because it is newly built and the roadbed is not yet solid, the train travels at only 30 kilometers per hour. This route runs parallel to the original Sujia Highway and the canal. The highway and canal are interwoven on both sides of the railway. The platforms at each station, with the exception of the offices, have been completed, but other facilities are still under construction. The area along the line can be said to be the most prosperous in Jiangsu and Zhejiang. As far as the eye can see, there are mulberry gardens, rice paddies, and lakes. At each station, residents came and went in droves, gathering outside the station to watch. Although yesterday was the first day of operation, there were approximately two hundred passengers boarding and alighting in each direction. The Sujia Highway bus was greatly affected. It is said that fares have been reduced by 20% of the original price. However, trains are stable and fast, and it is feared that most passengers will eventually abandon highway buses.

Touring the Lake in the Rain

At 10:15 AM, the train arrived in Jiaxing. They braved the rain to leave the station and first went to the railway bureau's nursery for a short rest, where they were warmly received by the field director. They then took a yacht to Yanyu Tower for a banquet. Wang Xianqiang, special commissioner of the Jiaxing district, was also invited to attend. During the banquet, Director Huang reported on the construction process, followed by a speech by Commissioner Wang, who stated that the opening of the Sujia line would further develop Jiaxing's transportation and promote the development of local construction. In the future, efforts should be made to develop local construction to promote the perfection of transportation. Finally, Jin Shixuan, representative of the Ministry of Railways, reported the Ministry of Railways' determination to complete the Jinghu-Hangzhou line. At 2:00 PM, they boarded small boats to tour the lake. At around 4:10 PM, Director Huang and the reporters returned to Shanghai on the Shanghai-Hangzhou train. Many reporters from Suzhou took the Sujia train back.

Start of Business

The Shanghai-Nanjing-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration issued a public announcement regarding the opening of the Sujia Railway: The Bureau is managing the Sujia Railway on behalf of the Ministry of Railways, and it will open for business on July 15th of this year. There will be four pairs of mixed trains between Jiaxing and Wuxian (Suzhou) each day, stopping at Wangjiangjing, Shengze, Pingwang, Bachai, Wujiang, and Xiangmen. In addition, to commemorate the opening, passengers who purchase one-way tickets within five days will have them stamped with a commemorative mark and will be exempt from the return fare within these five days. Suzhou to Xiangmen: (Express) 1st class 9 jiao, 2nd class 5 jiao, 3rd class 2 jiao 5 fen; (Ordinary) 1st class 3 jiao, 2nd class 2 jiao, 3rd class 1 jiao. To Wujiang: (Express) 1st class 1 yuan 4 jiao 5 fen, 2nd class 8 jiao 5 fen, 3rd class 4 jiao 5 fen; (Ordinary) 1st class 8 jiao 5 fen, 2nd class 5 jiao 5 fen, 3rd class 3 jiao. To Bachai: (Express) 1st class 1 yuan 8 jiao 5 fen, 2nd class 1 yuan 1 jiao 5 fen, 3rd class 6 jiao; (Ordinary) 1st class 2 yuan 2 jiao 5 fen, 2nd class 8 jiao 5 fen, 3rd class 4 jiao 5 fen. To Pingwang: (Express) 1st class 2 yuan 2 jiao 5 fen, 2nd class 1 yuan 4 jiao, 3rd class 7 jiao 5 fen; (Ordinary) 1st class 1 yuan 6 jiao 5 fen, 2nd class 1 yuan 1 jiao, 3rd class 6 jiao. To Shengze: (Express) 1st class 2 yuan 6 jiao 5 fen, 2nd class 1 yuan 6 jiao 5 fen, 3rd class 9 jiao; (Ordinary) 1st class 2 yuan 5 fen, 2nd class 1 yuan 3 jiao 5 fen, 3rd class 7 jiao 5 fen. Machine Manufacturers Association Petitions Shaanxi Provincial Government to Reward the Promotion of Domestic Goods in the Northwest; Requests Revision of Tax Rates and Exemption of Surcharges; Calculation Based on Cost Price, Do Not Arbitrarily Assess Value 109

The Shanghai Machine-Made Domestic Goods Manufacturers Association yesterday submitted a petition to the Shaanxi Provincial Government to reward the promotion of domestic goods in the Northwest. The original text states, "Submitting this petition with three points, earnestly requesting approval, in order to reward domestic goods and promote sales in the Northwest. We have received a letter from Sanyou Industrial Company, a member, stating, 'Our client, Zhongnan Store in Xi'an, Shaanxi, has been distributing domestic goods for a long time, and has been working hard to promote your company's products. However, the collection of special consumption taxes in Shaanxi Province is biased, with no fixed rules. Often, daily necessities of very little value are taxed at a rate exceeding the highest tax rate of modern national taxes, causing excellent domestic goods to fail to penetrate the interior and instead giving foreign goods the opportunity to dump, which is deeply regrettable. The Shanghai Machine-Made Domestic Goods Manufacturers Association is a group of domestic goods factories in our country, and your company has been a member for many years and has been committed to the domestic goods business for decades, so you must pay close attention to this. The fact that special taxes make it difficult for domestic goods to sell well is a difficulty that domestic goods factories in the Machine-Made Domestic Goods Manufacturers Association will encounter when promoting in the Northwest. Therefore, we have some humble opinions and ask you to convey them to the Machine-Made Domestic Goods Manufacturers Association to forward to the Shaanxi authorities to provide opportunities for Machine-Made Domestic Goods Manufacturers Association member factories to promote their products. The following points are listed for your consideration and implementation: (1) Re-determine the tax rate, and all products from Shanghai Machine-Made Domestic Goods Manufacturers Association member factories shall be assessed according to the production cost of goods in Shanghai, and taxed at a percentage to avoid the disadvantages of being biased. The price list shall be compiled and submitted by the Machine-Made Domestic Goods Manufacturers Association to avoid the malpractice of being biased; (2) Require exemption of surcharges to reward the smooth sale of domestic goods in the Northwest; (3) All products from Shanghai Machine-Made Domestic Goods Manufacturers Association member factories transported to the province shall be certified by the association to ensure that there are no fake goods or rebranding, so that customs inspection procedures can be eliminated after arriving in Shaanxi to benefit merchants (because local tax authorities often consider domestic goods to be fake goods). The above points should be forwarded to the Machine-Made Domestic Goods Manufacturers Association for handling, so that all domestic goods factories in Shanghai who are determined to develop the Northwest will quickly rise up and go to operate, and the heavy tax burden will be relieved by this move. We await your orders." Based on this, it is true that the rigorous collection of special taxes in Shaanxi Province, which increases the cost of goods, is one of the reasons why domestic goods are difficult to sell well in the Northwest. The points raised by the store are not without reason. This matter concerns the promotion of domestic goods, and a special letter is forwarded to you, requesting that your association submit a petition on its behalf to the extent possible to facilitate the development of domestic goods. The affection for our friendship has reached the association. After reviewing the points to be noted when revising the Shaanxi Special Consumption Tax Rate, point six states, "For goods not listed in this tax rate table, and other goods can be used for reference to levy taxes without being unfair, they shall be handled temporarily, but the name, origin, use, and cost price of the goods shall be described in detail and submitted for approval, and arbitrary valuation shall not be allowed to cause malpractice." From this, it can be seen that your province's Department of Finance is very strict in approving tax rates and is considerate of business conditions. However, the collecting agencies often do not follow the provisions but submit them for approval, and arbitrarily compare and levy taxes on goods that are not listed in the tax rate, which is inevitable. Otherwise, how could daily necessities of very little value be taxed at a rate exceeding the highest tax rate of modern tariffs? For example, the Wudi Soap Factory's No. 2 Butterfly Soap, with a selling price of four jiao per dozen, is subject to special consumption tax and surcharges on decorative items such as soap by the collecting agency to a huge amount of three jiao and six fen, which is obvious. Now, according to Sanyou Industrial Company, we have received a letter from Zhongnan Store in Xi'an requesting three points, which are indeed a way to reward domestic goods and promote sales in the Northwest. We should combine the list of members with a document and submit a petition, hoping that your government will approve it and eliminate the gap between government and business invisibly, and the future of domestic goods will be promising. I am overwhelmed with anticipation."

Ministry of Finance Issues Instructions on Stamp Tax on Notification Slips; Exempt for Those Not Used for Picking Up Goods 110

After the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Ministry of Finance to request instructions on whether notification slips used by the forwarding industry between the departure station company and the arrival station company should be stamped, yesterday the Ministry of Finance issued Tax No. 10051, stating, "The telegram and sample copies have been received. After investigation, if the forwarding industry has already provided a bill of lading to the consignor to pick up the goods at the arrival station, then the arrival station company can deliver the goods based on this bill of lading, so there is no need to create another notification slip. Moreover, the various items listed in this notification slip are no different from the provisions that should be included in the bill of lading, so it is possible to replace the bill of lading and give it to the customer to pick up the goods. However, since it is claimed that this notification slip is for the relationship between the departure station company and the arrival station company, and is not given to the customer for picking up goods, then in the future, if this notification slip is found, if it can immediately produce a bill of lading with the same content as the notification slip and has been stamped with sufficient stamp duty in accordance with the law, it can be exempted from stamp duty; otherwise, it should still be handled in accordance with item 13 of the tax rate table, Bill of Lading, to prevent taking advantage. Please forward these instructions for compliance."

Overseas Merchant Chen Bingding Talks About Improving Agriculture and Food; Methods of Planting Cassava and Mountain Millet 115

Overseas merchant Chen Bingding cares about the agriculture of his motherland. He recently submitted a memorial to the Ministry of Industry to reform planting methods. Because the original written opinion omitted the planting methods of cassava and mountain millet, he supplemented the conversation as follows: Our country has a vast territory, and there are barren mountains and remote areas everywhere. If we can use wasteland to plant mountain millet and cassava, it will greatly benefit the people's food supply. The planting methods of cassava and mountain millet are briefly described as follows: (1) Cassava (tapioca starch, sago) The original tree is seven or eight feet tall, and the trunk is straight. The seeds are available in Nanyang, Java, Taiwan, and Guangxi, and the price is very low. Each plant costs only one or two fen to transport to our country. If our people cultivate them themselves, half a fen is enough. The planting method is very easy. In the spring season, cut the branches of the original tree, half a foot long, use barren mountains, remove weeds, turn the soil more than a foot deep, and bury the cut branches into the soil about two inches deep, with a horizontal and vertical distance of one foot per plant. Following the Javanese planting method can avoid fertilization and often pay attention to weeding. After eight months, the harvest can be made, with each plant producing more than ten catties, followed by four or five catties, and the lowest grade also producing one or two catties. Bingding tried planting Javanese seeds in his hometown, and after nearly a year, each plant yielded up to thirteen catties, with excellent quality, far superior to our country's sweet potatoes. Moreover, the tree reproduces extremely quickly. If a family plants ten plants, then after eight months, they can be divided into more than one hundred and sixty plants, and after another eight months, they can be divided into more than two thousand plants. (2) Mountain Millet (dry rice) Use barren mountains, remove weeds, and turn the soil more than half a foot deep. In early spring, first use sharpened bamboo to dig holes in the soil, about an inch deep, and place four or five seeds in each hole, cover them with soil evenly, and the horizontal and vertical distance of each hole is four or five inches wide. Following the Javanese planting method can also avoid fertilization and only add weeding. After four months, the harvest can be made. The rice quality is harder than paddy rice. After harvesting, it is best to leave the stalks in place and burn them to nourish the land. Java has mountain millet seeds, and the price is not expensive, with each dan worth about eight yuan in our country. The above two foods are easy to sow and the cost is light. Once reproduced, they will greatly benefit the future of the people's food supply, and perhaps the tens of millions of yuan of food imports that are leaked every year can be salvaged somewhat.

Postal Savings Bureau Decides to Add Safe Deposit Box Services 116

After deciding to add safe deposit box services, the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau yesterday sent letters to various institutions and organizations, and also stipulated rental rules and prices. The details are as follows:

Letter to Various Institutions

Regarding the matter of offering safety deposit boxes, Shanghai's prosperity is unmatched in the country, and wealth from all directions converges here. Gold glitters, easily tempting the covetous hearts of petty thieves. Daytime robbery is a constant reminder of the need for vigilance in the city. Although local police patrols are generally thorough, it is difficult for people to be completely prepared. Therefore, the safety deposit box business arises from social needs. The rental fees are limited, but the safety of property is ensured. Ordinary people are eagerly renting them as a way to ensure safety. Our municipal government agencies, as well as the deeds, contracts, duplicate keys, valuables, etc. of public and private organizations are all important. Rather than building separate vaults or installing large iron cabinets, which would cost a lot of money and still not completely solve the safety problem, it would be wiser to use safety deposit boxes as storage places. Our bureau moved to the new Construction Building at the beginning of last month and added the safety deposit box business. We have already made a public announcement and invite your attention. Our bureau is located next to the police station, a prime location. The safety deposit vault we built has a precise structure and a spacious scale. It is equipped with 2,000 steel-made safety deposit boxes of various sizes, most of which have inner boxes. They are sturdily manufactured and have a novel style. Deposits and withdrawals are convenient, rental fees are low, and procedures are simple. In addition to providing rental services for individuals and companies, we are willing to serve various institutions and organizations wholeheartedly. We ask for your consideration.

Rental Rules

Article 1: The rental of safety deposit boxes by this bureau is subject to the Shanghai Municipal Safety Deposit Box Rental Regulations. However, those which should be specified by this bureau are specially stipulated in these regulations. Article 2: The rental fees for safety deposit boxes are detailed in the attached table. Article 3: The key deposit is set at 20 yuan in national currency per box. Article 4: The handling fee for reissuing a key deposit receipt is set at 50 cents in national currency. Article 5: If the renter loses one key, in addition to following Article 11 of the Shanghai Municipal Safety Deposit Box Rental Regulations, the renter shall immediately return the remaining key to this bureau and pay a compensation fee of 6 yuan in national currency. If the renter loses all the keys, the renter shall compensate this bureau 20 yuan in national currency, and this bureau will replace the lock to avoid danger. Article 6: If the items in the safety deposit box need to be sealed and stored by this bureau due to the circumstances in Article 17 of the Shanghai Municipal Safety Deposit Box Rental Regulations, the storage fee shall be calculated by this bureau in accordance with the regulations. Article 7: If the renter does not return both keys and retrieve the items after the rental period has expired or the rental has been terminated, the overdue rental fee shall be calculated as six months if it is less than six months, and as one year if it is more than six months. Article 8: These rules may be modified at any time without notice.

Rental Prices

Dimensions (in feet): A1, Height 5 inches, Width 5.25 inches, Depth 12 inches, Rental fee: 2 yuan for half a year, 3 yuan for a full year. A2, Height 5 inches, Width 5.25 inches, Depth 20 inches, Rental fee: 3 yuan for half a year, 4 yuan for a full year. A3, Height 5 inches, Width 5.25 inches, Depth 24 inches, Rental fee: 3 yuan for half a year, 5 yuan for a full year. B, Height 5 inches, Width 10.875 inches, Depth 20 inches, Rental fee: 5 yuan for half a year, 8 yuan for a full year. Forcible Relocation of Shantytowns in Eastern Shanghai: Municipal Council Agrees to Flexible Handling. Shantytown Residents Appeal to All Parties Again, Requesting the Speedy Construction of Public Housing. 118

Regarding the case of the Public Concession Municipal Council forcing the relocation of shantytowns in Eastern Shanghai, after mediation by Yu Qiaqing, the Municipal Council Board of Directors has agreed to handle it flexibly. Shantytown residents have once again appealed to all parties. The details are as follows:

Mr. Yu Mediates for Flexible Handling

Based on the request of the shantytown residents, Chinese Director Yu Qiaqing conducted mediation at the Municipal Council Board of Directors meeting yesterday afternoon. The following measures were decided: (1) No further increase in shantytowns shall be allowed; (2) One person shall be designated as responsible for guaranteeing every ten households. If any additional construction is discovered, all ten households will be demolished; (3) The shantytown residents shall conduct a survey of the total population and report it to the Municipal Council; (4) Fully responsible representatives shall be designated in each district. All of the above have been accepted by both parties. Therefore, the General Affairs Department of the Municipal Council, which previously stated that demolition would resume on the 15th, did not send personnel yesterday because the matter had reached a stage of resolution.

Chamber of Commerce Petitions the Municipal Government for Negotiations

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce submitted a petition to the municipal government yesterday, stating, "Regarding the matter of submitting a petition, the chamber recently received a joint letter from the shantytown residents of Eastern Shanghai, stating that the concession authorities have set a deadline for the demolition of their shacks, leaving them with nowhere to live, and requesting assistance. It is said that there are nearly 50 families who are facing this deadline for demolition, while the letter from the shantytown residents this time claims that there are more than 10,000 households, which will become a serious problem for the poor people living in this city. This matter cannot be ignored. However, merely making empty appeals for postponement may be rejected by the concession authorities. After careful consideration, the only way to solve the problem is for your government to discuss the matter with the Municipal Council and clarify the measures to be taken. We will gradually increase the number of public housing units each year. Each year, a certain number of public housing units will be added, and the concession will limit the demolition of a certain number of shantytowns, so that there will be a way to accommodate them and they will not have to worry about losing their homes. For the time being, please postpone the demolition. Is this appropriate? We hereby submit a document to your government for review and approval, as it is in the public interest."

Shantytown Residents Appeal to All Parties Again

Yesterday, the shantytown residents sent representatives Zhang Buyun, Yin Yifu, Tang Anping, etc., to report the situation to the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce. They were received by Secretary Zhu Boyuan, who advised the shantytown residents to live in peace. In the afternoon, they went to the First Special District Citizens' Federation to petition, where they were received by Chen Jiufeng. The shantytown residents said that the Municipal Council's move was illegal: (1) Because Yanshan Road has not been built, if they want to force the relocation, they should build it first and install the utility poles; (2) The landowner must build houses before they can order the relocation; (3) The Municipal Council should build public housing before they can force the relocation. Mr. Chen replied that he would negotiate for a postponement of the demolition and urge the Municipal Council to build public housing, starting with registering rickshaw pullers to improve the lives of workers.

Zhou Zuomin and Others Take Over the China Shipbuilding Factory, Change to a Limited Liability Company, and Appoint Sheng Pingru as Manager. 119

The Greater China Shipbuilding Factory (located east of Dinghai Bridge, near the Fishery Market, founded by shipbuilding expert Yang Junsheng, has been in operation for more than ten years. It has had excellent achievements in the past, such as the Xin Dada Wheel of Dada Company, the Tianxing Wheel of Tianjin Shipping Company, and the Jiangxi Zhongzheng Bridge (over 1,000 feet long), all of which were built by the factory. Therefore, its technology, materials, and workmanship have long been trusted by Chinese shipowners. However, it did not pay much attention to business management, which led to the factory's grounding last year. As a result, it owed more than 530,000 yuan to various parties. After several lawsuits, the court convened a meeting of creditors and, in accordance with the bankruptcy law, repaid the creditors a certain percentage. The creditors agreed, and the dispute came to an end. The machinery, equipment, and various projects of the Greater China Shipbuilding Factory are very complete, and it is the best of the Chinese-owned shipyards in Shanghai. It is a pity that it was suspended due to debt. Mr. Yang is willing to transfer the factory to Chinese people to continue operating, and has negotiated with Zhou Zuomin, the general director of Jin Cheng Bank, Fan Xudong, the owner of Jiuda Refined Salt Company, and Lu Zuofu, the director of the Sichuan Construction Department and the general manager of Minsheng Industrial Company, to take over the new factory. Mr. Yang and Zhou Zuomin were classmates in Dongying (Japan). Now, Zhou, Fan, Lu, and others believe that shipbuilding is the largest industry, and Shanghai should have a large-scale, Chinese-owned commercial shipyard to benefit shipping. Therefore, they have agreed. The procedures for taking over and the formal contract have been signed by both parties, and the factory will be taken over immediately. However, the new shareholders have decided to make the factory a joint-stock company, so the name has also been changed to "China Shipbuilding Machinery Factory Co., Ltd." It will be reorganized. Zhou Zuomin will serve as the chairman of the new factory, and Fan Xudong and Lu Zuofu will serve as managing directors. Shipbuilding engineering expert Sheng Pingru has been specially appointed as the manager, and it has been decided that the position of assistant manager will still be held by the original founder, Yang Junsheng. This was decided on the 1st of this month. The handover is currently in progress. The manager's office will be located on the upper floor of Jin Cheng Bank. Manager Sheng has negotiated with the Huangpu River Conservancy Board and agreed to dredge the waterline in front of the factory to facilitate the construction of large ships. From now on, the factory will have the strong financial power of major industrialists and financiers, as well as the expert planning of Sheng Pingru. The future is truly limitless. In the shortest possible time, it has been decided to add a dry dock and expand the business. This is truly good news for China's shipping industry.
