Cotton Yarn 186

Multiple Bearish Trades Emerge, Yarn Prices Plunge, Yarn Prices Drop Three to Four Yuan in Two Days, Still Above One Yuan 187

The cotton yarn market has been hit hard, and the price drop is intensifying. This is mainly because after a period of rapid price increases, customer purchases have completely stopped, leading to market instability. Furthermore, foreign firms and manufacturers, seeing little actual trading activity and high benchmark yarn prices, are collectively selling short. As a result, the recent price decline has become even more severe. In the afternoon, securities brokers released large volumes of bearish positions, and many others followed suit, causing the market to collapse. These sudden rises and falls are entirely due to the volatile sentiments of speculators.

Benchmark Yarn Starts to Fall

At the opening of the benchmark yarn market, prices for all months were stagnant due to the high prices and the clearing of most speculative short positions. Consequently, there was a lack of buyers in the market. However, the market situation changed dramatically after the opening, with strong selling pressure and ample supply of yarn. As Osaka's Three Grades of Yarn saw declines, buyers became even scarcer. Prices for all months plummeted by 1.3, 1.4, 1.5, and 1.6 yuan. By the third closing, it was reported that spot yarn business was very slow, further weakening market sentiment. As a result, near-month contracts fell by 1.5 to 2 yuan compared to the previous day's closing price, while distant-month contracts fell by 0.5, 0.6, and 0.8 yuan. At the afternoon opening, near-month contracts stabilized, while distant-month contracts rose by 0.3 and 0.4 yuan. However, after the opening, incoming Osaka Three Grades of Yarn cables showed continuous declines, prompting securities firms and gold merchants to sell off, leading to a further market collapse. Prices continued to fall until the lowest closing price was reached. As a result, prices for all months fell by 1.4 to 1.69 yuan compared to the morning closing price. It was noted that Da Chang sold 3,250 bales, Tai Chang 1,100 bales, Tong Ji 1,950 bales, Ji Feng 1,100 bales, Yi Ji 1,750 bales, Ming De 800 bales, Xing Chang 850 bales, Ren Feng 1,200 bales, Chang Feng 2,800 bales, Yong Da 1,850 bales, Tong He 1,100 bales, and Xin Cheng 4,050 bales. On the buying side, Cheng Ji bought 1,000 bales, Da Fu 2,850 bales, Ju Xing 2,200 bales, Yu Da 1,550 bales, Jin Chang 2,100 bales, He Xing 2,900 bales, Shen Ji 2,150 bales, Da Chang Cheng 1,150 bales, and Sheng Yuan 700 bales. The daily high, low, and closing prices are listed below.

Spot Yarn Weakens in the Morning, Recovers in the Afternoon

Spot yarn sales are sluggish. It is noted that the total purchases from various firms throughout the day amounted to 585 yuan. Morning prices saw a drop of 2 yuan for yarn and 5 yuan for thread. In the afternoon, yarn prices rose by 1 yuan and thread prices by 2 yuan. Purchase amounts for each firm are as follows:

Inland: 440; Fellow traders: 140; Anqing: 5

The cotton market is weakening, with a sharp price decline. This is largely due to the initial rise and subsequent fall of US cotton, resulting in only a slight increase. Southern cotton farmers are still selling short, easing market sentiment. Additionally, the yarn market is trending downward, and in the afternoon, securities firms and gold merchants released large volumes of positions, causing the market to gradually decline. Distant-month contracts have broken through the 3-yuan barrier.

This Month's Cotton Down 0.85 Yuan

At the opening of the benchmark cotton market, US cotton first rose and then retreated, resulting in a small increase of 3 to 6 points. It is generally expected that the upward trend can be temporarily halted. Although Indian cotton rose by 1 to 2 rupees, attention is focused on US cotton. Osaka's Three Grades of Cotton fell by 0.6 to 0.7 yuan, leading to peaceful market sentiment. Near-month contracts fell by 0.15 to 0.4 yuan, while distant-month contracts also fell by 0.2 to 0.3 yuan. Given the unfavorable momentum, speculative traders rushed to sell. The second and third trading sessions remained weak. However, new cotton rebounded by 0.1 to 0.2 yuan, and at the closing, old cotton recovered slightly. As a result, old cotton fell by 0.25 to 0.3 yuan compared to the previous day's closing price, while new cotton fell by 0.05 to 0.1 yuan. At the afternoon opening, the market sentiment for old cotton turned upward, while new cotton fell by 0.05 to 0.15 yuan. The second and third trading sessions were uneventful. However, as the closing approached, the price decline intensified, as bond and financial firms took profits and released large volumes of positions, causing a sudden market slump. Old cotton broke through the 9-yuan mark, falling by 0.3 to 0.4 yuan across the board. New cotton fell below the 3-yuan barrier. As a result, prices for all months fell by 0.2, 0.4, and 0.5 yuan compared to the morning closing price. It was noted that Yong Da sold 2,000 dan, Da Chang 3,600 dan, Ming Hua 2,000 dan, Ming De 2,000 dan, Yu Da 2,000 dan, Da Fu 3,100 dan, Da Feng 2,800 dan, Yuan... 4,500 dan, Yi Kang 3,000 dan, Shen Chang 1,200 dan, Xing Chang 1,200 dan, Cheng Ji 1,700 dan, and De Da 1,600 dan. On the buying side, Yuan Xing Chang bought 3,600 dan, Xin Cheng 3,600 dan, Tong Ji 6,000 dan, Zhen Da 1,700 dan, He Xing 4,200 dan, Shen Ji 8,000 dan, Da Chang Cheng 2,500 dan,... 2,600 dan, Yong Chang 1,200 dan, and Tong He 1,300 dan. The daily high, low, and closing prices are listed below.

Demand for Spot Cotton Remains Sluggish

Spot cotton consumption remains mediocre, with sluggish mill demand. Sources: Yao cotton 340 bales, Tianjin American cotton 6.4.00. Gongda Mill purchased 100 pieces. Spot delivery to the factory: Tianjin American cotton 6.275. Gongda Mill purchased 100 pieces. Spot delivery to the factory.

Both Eastern and Western Districts Benefit from Rainfall, US Cotton Does Not Rise Much, Three Grades of Yarn and Cotton Also Fall 188

Yesterday, US cotton opened strongly, with positive news from Liverpool. Dealers, brokers, and foreign firms bought in, driving prices up by 12 to 15 points for all months. However, as bullish traders quickly closed their positions, and New Orleans, local firms, and cotton farmers sold short, prices retreated slightly. Parts of both the eastern and western districts benefited from rainfall. It is expected that tomorrow's weather report will be favorable, especially in Texas, which has dampened bullish sentiment. It is widely believed that the damage in parts of Georgia and the Carolinas has been alleviated by the recent rainfall. Trading volume was low. July contracts were firm, with spot prices up 4 points and futures prices up 3 to 5 points. British cotton spot prices rose by 6 pence, and futures prices rose by 6 to 8 points. Indian cotton was bought by Japanese firms, and bullish traders closed their positions. July and August contracts for White Raw Cotton were actively bought by Liverpool, making them even stronger. Plain cotton rose/fell by 0.25 to 1.25 rupees, Oomra rose by 0.25 to 2 rupees, and White Raw Cotton rose by 1.75 to 2.25 rupees. Original telegram recorded on the 14th.

According to a Bombay telegram, the opening forecast for the April/May contracts of White Raw Cotton on the 15th was 226.5 rupees, down 1.75 rupees from the previous day.

Osaka telegram on the 15th: Three Grades of Yarn futures fell by 2.6 to 3.7 yuan, with near-month contracts at 213.3 yuan and distant-month contracts at 207.2 yuan. Cotton futures fell by 0.8 to 1.55 yuan, with near-month contracts at 72.15 yuan and distant-month contracts at 65.85 yuan.

Grains Wheat Prices Retreat Slightly, Flour Futures See Significant Liquidation 189

Yesterday's wheat market saw prices open steady in the morning, followed by a gradual decline. Opening prices for foreign wheat were based on Chicago, down about 0.3 to 0.5 yuan, and Canada, down 0.1 yuan. Due to cautious market sentiment from both bulls and bears, trading volume was low, resulting in limited price movement for all months. The market remained stable during the afternoon opening. However, as traders gradually sold off their holdings due to the inability to raise spot wheat prices, most of them sold through the exchange. These sellers seemed to believe in the realities of the market, which eased market sentiment and led to a gradual decline in opening prices. Market observers speculate that if the flour market turns sluggish, the wheat market will undoubtedly follow suit. The spot wheat market saw active arrivals, but mill demand was average. Bidding prices were generally reduced by 0.02 yuan. Opening prices were: Chuzhou wheat at 4.5 yuan, Mingguang Shaheji Guandian wheat at 4.53 yuan, Zhuzhen wheat at 4.46 yuan, Dongge wheat at 4.45 yuan, Puzhen wheat at 4.42 yuan, and Huaian wheat at 4.48 yuan. Fufeng shipped 6,000 bags, and Shen Da shipped 3,000 bags.

The US wheat market saw increased rainfall and cooler weather. The forecast of cooler weather and rain has raised hopes that the drought may be alleviated. As a result, although the US and Canada continued to report damages, it had little impact, and trading was relatively quiet. The market is waiting for a more definitive outlook.

Chicago Wheat July 13 July 14 Change

September 103.875 102.125 Down 1.750

December 105.250 102.500 Down 1.750

Canadian Wheat

October 91.250 90.625 Down 0.625

Yesterday, the flour market saw limited-price openings for all months in both the morning and afternoon. While formal trading was slow, there were significant off-market liquidations. Due to the easing of the wheat market, floating longs and some clients were willing to exit their positions in the off-market, with near-month contracts down only 0.04 to 0.05 yuan, August contracts down only 0.02 to 0.03 yuan, and subsequent months also down only 0.03 to 0.05 yuan. This situation indicates that the market situation has significantly eased, and it is rumored that the Social Affairs Bureau's price limits will soon be lifted.

Thin Rice Sales Are Smooth, Prices Remain Firm 190

(South Shanghai) Yesterday's supplies from various sources were still limited to 2,400 to 2,500 piculs of Grade 12 and 13 rice. However, sales in this area were slow. Despite Lianqing and Qingdao firms purchasing over 1,000 bags of thin rice, the downward trend persisted. As a result, prices for thick early japonica and thin rice all weakened slightly. Du Yang Jian's arrival and sales were both low, and market prices remained unchanged.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, supplies of Grade 12 and 13 rice from various locations along the river arrived, and the market sold off existing stocks. Fresh white japonica rice saw slight movement, with prices remaining stable. Old stocks remained sluggish, with prices down slightly. Thin rice arrivals were low and sales were active, with prices holding firm. White Yuan prices weakened by 0.03 to 0.04 yuan, and prices for high-quality Yang Jian rice weakened slightly. Prices for medium and low-quality rice were down by a small margin. Prices for Port Guest Jian rice weakened by a small margin. Prices for all other types of rice showed a downward trend.

Hot and Humid Weather Leads to Rice Hoarding Release 191

Due to the lack of consistent demand from local traders, the price of glutinous rice has been steadily declining. Yesterday, traders, guest vendors, and hoarders were eager to sell off their inventory, leading to price reductions. As a result, prices for all types of rice continued to fall. In recent days, the price of mid-grade rice has fallen by nearly 1 yuan, while the price of high-quality rice has fallen by more than 0.5 to 0.6 yuan. Due to the price reductions, inland firms have shown some interest, purchasing over 2,000 bags of Xiangjing and Zhongguan Gan early and late rice. Local traders also lowered prices to compete, leading to a slightly more active market. Total daily trading volume was around 5,000 bags.

Silk and Tea US and Japanese Silk Markets Both Decline 192

Yesterday, the overseas silk markets remained stable. The New York and Yokohama silk markets did not see any significant price fluctuations. New York spot prices fell slightly by 0.01 yuan, and futures prices fell slightly by 0.005 yuan. Yokohama spot prices fell by 3 yuan, and futures prices rose by 1 yuan. Prices for goods of Chinese origin in New York and quotations in the Lyon silk market remained unchanged. Both domestic and overseas silk markets remained firm and stagnant, with very little trading activity.

Yesterday, the rayon market saw active buying interest. However, hoarders were hesitant to sell, leading to moderate trading activity. Prices for 120-denier Sunlight brand were around 400 yuan for over 20 boxes, and prices for 120-denier Sky Bridge brand were over 400 yuan. Due to limited inventory, traders were reluctant to sell at reduced prices. A major local firm, feeling that its inventory was low and the market was stable, ordered 200 boxes of 120-denier bright Italian Sniade No. 3 goods from Carlowitz & Co., at a price of 100 yuan per bill of lading. The firm's asking price was also 100 yuan.

Yichang Black Tea Actively Bought, Tunxi Zhenmei Sells Well at Firm Prices 193

Yichang black tea has recently been shipped to Shanghai for sale. Yesterday, Jardine Matheson & Co. and Zhongxin Chang Tea Firm agreed to a deal for over 700 boxes, with prices ranging from 67 to 87 yuan. The market remained stable. Qining black tea continued to see active sales for high and mid-grade goods, while low-grade goods remained sluggish. Due to the surge in arrivals, Huaxiang broken leaf tea prices continued to decline. As for the green tea market, yesterday, various foreign firms, seeing that inventories of early-spring Tunxi Zhenmei were low, actively purchased them, resulting in a total trading volume of over 1,000 boxes, with Tianyu, Jinlong, and Tongfu being the most active. Selling prices ranged from 80 to 86 yuan, slightly firmer than before. Trading in other types of Zhenmei was relatively slow. In addition, due to the surge in daily arrivals of Sui'an Zhenmei, and its inferior quality, sales remained sluggish. From this perspective, the prospects for second-flush green tea are not optimistic.

Page 18

Piece Goods Dye Works Are Eager to Purchase Fine Cloth 194

With benchmark yarn and cotton prices declining for consecutive days, market sentiment has gradually weakened. However, due to the fact that mills are still unable to make a profit at current selling prices, and dye works are placing large orders for colored cloth for July and August, most mills have already replenished their stocks of white cloth from Japanese factories. As a result, mill stocks have already been sold. Dye works are also eagerly purchasing large quantities of local machine-made fine cloth this month, making deliveries very urgent. Therefore, market momentum remains firm. Demand for colored cloth from the Sichuan and Yangtze firms is most urgent this month. Due to the new Yangtze River shipping regulations, which calculate freight based on the size of the container, and which are scheduled to take effect on the 16th, various traders are rushing to ship their goods before the deadline, leading to extremely frequent cargo traffic recently. Yesterday, firms along the Yangtze River, such as Hankou, Changsha, and Nanchang, shipped over 200 pieces of white cloth, fine cloth, fine twill, and coarse cloth, as well as over 300 pieces of broadcloth, tribute silk, blue cloth, plain twill, and gray twill. In addition to the Yangtze firms, businesses in Bengbu and Anhui also saw improved sales of colored cloth, white cloth, fine cloth, and fine twill. Sales in all other areas were sluggish.

Sugar Market Guangdong Sugar Bidding Is Slow 195

Yesterday's sugar market trend was stable, with less trading activity. The association's price list for goods such as Grade 24 coarse granulated sugar, white sugar, and Dongbai Nos. 4, 8, and 9 spot goods, as well as transit goods, remained unchanged, with few transactions. Prices for goods from local factories such as Bai Jin Xin, Da Hua, and Zhen Ji also did not fluctuate. The price list included 136 bags of Chaozhou firm's Chung Ti Qing, at 10.9 yuan; 110 bags of secondary Zhuang Zhi Yang, at 11.5 yuan; 240 bags of high and medium Zhuang Zhi Yang, at 14.6 yuan; and dozens of bags of secondary Zhi Chi, at 11.1 yuan. It is reported that Shantou exchange rates remain unstable, with rumors of a return to 1,310 yuan.

The joint venture company held its second bidding session for Guangdong sugar this week. The total allocation was 7,357 bags, and the bid prices remained unchanged. The resulting trading volume was low, as firms had already made significant purchases last week. Yesterday, 400 bags of City Center Granulated White were sold at 19.3 yuan, and 50 bags of No. 4 Mianbai were sold at 20.6 yuan. The remaining products, such as Wuyang Coarse White from factories in Shunde, Dongguan, and Qu Creek, did not sell at the original prices.

New Golden Lily Flowers Will Have Uniform Market Price Industry Initiates Company Reorganization 197

Since the introduction of new golden lily flowers, goods from Xuzhou Zhongxing and other sources have been arriving in Shanghai in increasing quantities. Yesterday, the first batch of 199 bags of Zhongxing lily flowers was transferred to the warehouse for sale. Northern goods industry members had previously formed a public company last year to standardize prices and eliminate competition. It is now reported that industry leaders are initiating a reorganization of the company, following the example of last year. A total of 76 shares will be issued, with over 20 companies participating.

Yin Yu 198

By Zihan

After Emperor Huizong and Emperor Qinzong of the Song Dynasty were captured by the Jin Dynasty, Emperor Gaozong crossed the Yangtze River and established the capital in Hangzhou. The lost territories in the north were never recovered, and only half of the country was preserved. During the reign of Emperor Lizong, the appointment of the useless Jia Sidao further worsened the situation. At this time, the Jin Dynasty was already weakening, while the Mongols in the north—under the name of Yuan—were rising in power and eventually destroyed the Jin Dynasty.

After Emperor Lizong died, Emperor Qingzong ascended the throne and continued to employ Jia Sidao. In the fifth year of Emperor Qingzong's reign, the Yuan Dynasty ordered General Bayan to lead a large army to attack the Song Dynasty. They besieged Xiangyang in northern Hubei for five years, and Jia Sidao did not send troops to relieve the siege. The defending general, Lü Wenhuan, had no choice but to surrender. After capturing Xiangyang, Bayan led his troops to take Hanyang and Wuchang, also successfully seizing them. Bayan ordered his men to guard Hubei, while he and Azhu led their troops and warships down the river to capture Hangzhou, the capital of the Southern Song Dynasty.

At that time, Wen Tianxiang was secluded in Wenshan, Jiangxi, reading books. Upon hearing that the Yuan army was advancing eastward down the river, he used patriotic rhetoric to inspire the local heroes to raise an army to defend the emperor. However, the treacherous minister Chen Yizhong, the Right Chancellor, did not want Wen Tianxiang to come to Hangzhou and ordered him to station his troops in Nanchang, Jiangxi. Before long, the Yuan army swept all before them and reached the lower reaches of the Yangtze River. Hangzhou was in a state of panic and finally summoned Wen Tianxiang to bring his troops to Hangzhou. In August of the first year of Emperor Gongzong's reign, Wen Tianxiang arrived in Hangzhou. In September, he was appointed Prefect of Suzhou by imperial decree. On October 15th, Wen Tianxiang arrived in Suzhou. At that time, the Yuan army had already besieged Changzhou.

Wen Tianxiang ordered his subordinates Zhu Hua and Ma Shilong to lead the Guangxi troops, and Yin Yu to lead the Jiangxi troops, to join Zhang Quan's Huai army to relieve Changzhou.

However, Zhang Quan was a useless fellow and was also at odds with the other generals. On October 26th, they encountered the Yuan army at Henglin Yuqiao, and a fierce battle ensued. Ma Shilong was killed in action, and Zhang Quan did not come to his aid, fleeing back to Wumu. Wumu was where Zhu Hua was stationed, and Zhu Hua wanted to set up barricades and dig trenches, but Zhang Quan refused to allow it.

On the 27th, the Yuan army attacked Wumu, and Zhu Hua opened the camp gate and led his Guangxi troops to fight the Yuan army. The battle lasted from morning to afternoon, with heavy casualties on both sides, but no decisive victory was achieved. The Yuan army also retreated.

That night, the Yuan army circled around to the back of the mountain to attack the Jiangxi camp of Yin Yu. Yin Yu was a general in the Jiangxi military administration and had followed Wen Tianxiang since he raised his army. Yin Yu was straightforward and skilled in martial arts. He often said, "The Zhao imperial family was misguided in trusting Qin Hui and harming Yue Wumu Wang, which prevented the recovery of lost territory. Later, Emperor Lizong employed the traitor Jia Sidao, making the country's affairs even worse. Without loyal and righteous people, how can the country prosper? I, Yin Yu, have a strong will and have mastered martial arts. Given the opportunity, I will surely serve the country."

Later, Yin Yu heard that Wen Tianxiang had raised an army in Jizhou, Jiangxi, to defend the emperor. He was overjoyed and said, "Master Wen is a good man. Now he is raising an army to save the country. Who else should I, Yin Yu, sell this body and these skills to but to Master Wen?"

Therefore, Yin Yu bid farewell to his family and, alone on horseback, went to Jizhou to join Wen Tianxiang.

Wen Tianxiang was pleased with Yin Yu's dignified appearance and imposing presence. However, Wen Tianxiang was still unsure of Yin Yu's loyalty and tested him, saying, "The Yuan army is strong, and our efforts to defend the emperor may not succeed. We may even suffer a major defeat and lose our lives. General, this is a dangerous matter, and you must think it over."

Yin Yu replied loudly, "Master Wen, do not underestimate Yin Yu. If a true man cannot establish merit and achieve success, and use this useful body to serve the country, would he simply spend his life guarding his wife? In coming here, Yin Yu has already stopped considering life and death as separate matters, and considers us as one. We are doing this for the country!"

Wen Tianxiang was overjoyed and patted Yin Yu's back, saying, "General, you are truly a loyal and righteous man!"

Yin Yu followed Wen Tianxiang in Nanchang, Hangzhou, and Suzhou.

That day, upon receiving Wen Tianxiang's order, he went to Changzhou with Zhu Hua to relieve the siege. Zhu Hua set up his main camp on the main road of Wumu, while Yin Yu set up his camp on the key pass behind the mountain.

On the 27th of October, in the first year of Emperor Gongzong's reign, when the Yuan army attacked Wumu and engaged in a fierce battle with Zhu Hua, Yin Yu wanted to lead his troops to relieve the siege, but the road behind the mountain was too important, and he dared not leave his post without authorization. In case of any mishap, what would he do! He was anxious and paced back and forth on his horse, clenching his teeth and gnawing, holding his spear, watching the dust billowing in front of the mountain, and listening to the battle cries shaking the earth in front of the mountain. Yin Yu's life was truly unbearable that day.

In the afternoon, the Yuan army retreated, and Zhu Hua led his troops back to camp. Yin Yu also breathed a sigh of relief. However, Yin Yu still dared not be careless and ordered, "Although the enemy soldiers are northerners, they are still just as cunning in their tactics. Although they have retreated today, they may very well return. We must be even more careful tonight. Tonight, no one is allowed to remove their armor, and the horses are not allowed to remove their saddles. Be vigilant!"

As Yin Yu had expected, that night, the Yuan army divided its 100,000 troops into two groups. One group attacked Zhu Hua's main camp on the main road of Wumu, while the other group attacked Yin Yu's camp on the key pass behind the mountain, preventing the Song troops from supporting each other.

Yin Yu was in the central command tent, reading under the candlelight, when he heard distant shouts and the neighing of horses. He knew that the Yuan army had come to raid the camp. At the same time, a hidden sentinel came to report that the Yuan army was raiding the camp. Fortunately, no one had removed their armor, and the horses had not been unsaddled. Upon Yin Yu's command, the entire camp was roused, and the camp gates were opened. Yin Yu mounted his horse, raised his spear, charged out of the camp gate, and met the Yuan army head-on.

The 50,000 Yuan soldiers carried lanterns and torches, making it as bright as day. They came sweeping down the mountains and plains. Seeing such a sight, even the bravest would be terrified. Therefore, even before the battle began, the camps of Zeng Tong, Hu Yu, Xie Yun, and Zeng Yu collapsed, Zhang Quan's army fled, and Zhu Hua's troops were cut off by the Yuan army and could not provide support. Only Yin Yu and his 500 men were left to face the 50,000 Yuan soldiers sweeping down the mountains and plains.

Seeing that several camps had collapsed, Yin Yu cursed through gritted teeth, "These cowardly cowards!" He then said to his 500 men, "Brothers, my good friends, you have always been of one mind with me. Today is our good opportunity to serve the country! Brothers, even if we are down to one man, we must fight the enemy. Killing one enemy is enough, killing two is profit! Brothers, give it your all!"

The 500 men replied in unison, "We will be with the general in life and death!"

Yin Yu shouted, "Good! You are truly Yin Yu's good brothers! Good! Let us charge forward!"

The 500 men shouted in unison, spurred on their warhorses, and charged towards the Yuan army like a whirlwind. Yin Yu was in the lead, and with each thrust of his spear, he knocked several Yuan soldiers off their horses. Like a cloud of fire, the 500 men plunged into the Yuan army's ranks.

Bayan was overseeing the battle in the central command, and when he saw the front army scatter to the sides, he hurriedly spurred on his horse to take a look. He saw a Song general with several hundred Song soldiers, like a pack of fierce tigers, charging left and right in the enemy ranks, as if entering an empty field.

Bayan was shocked and quickly raised his saber, spurred on his horse to meet him, and shouted, "Stop, General of the Southern Dynasty! Look at my Great Yuan's 50,000 soldiers here, and another 50,000 soldiers in front of the mountain, surrounding you on all sides. General, what can your few hundred men accomplish? Why not dismount and surrender to the Great Yuan? Once you take the Southern Dynasty's lands, you will be granted land and ennobled. It will not be lacking for you. General, what do you think?"

Hearing this, Yin Yu cursed, "You vile dog, shut your mouth! I am a Song man in life, and a Song ghost in death! Even if I die in battle, I will not surrender. You vile dog, do not think that I have few men. My 500 men will still kill you until men and horses are overturned."

After saying this, Yin Yu thrust his spear and charged straight at Bayan. Bayan turned his horse slightly and retreated, waving his command flag, tightening the encirclement of 50,000 men. Unable to kill Bayan, Yin Yu could only engage in a mixed battle with his 500 men in the Yuan army's ranks. The Yuan soldiers grew in number, and Yin Yu fought more and more bravely, fighting all through the night.

Yin Yu saw that his troops were gradually dwindling, and that both he and his horse were bearing many wounds. His armor was soaked in blood, and his horse was also covered in blood. However, Yin Yu had no intention of retreating and continued to fight with all his might. As Yin Yu fought on, he grew exhausted and could no longer hold on. Knowing that the situation was dire, he cried out, "Ancestors of the Great Song, Master Wen, Yin Yu is exhausted..." Before he could finish speaking, he spat out blood and fell off his horse!

Yin Yu was dead, but the remaining troops under his command continued to fight to the death. The battle lasted until dawn, with the Yuan soldiers leaving corpses strewn across the field and blood flowing like rivers. Only four of the 500 men survived, and none of them surrendered. This battle at Wumu truly terrified the Yuan soldiers.

Darwin and His Theory of Evolution 199

— Guo Xuan

(Charles Darwin 1809——1882)

In the first chapter of the old biblical Genesis, it is recorded the story of God creating man. It says that God first created the sun, moon, stars, mountains, rivers, grass, and trees, and finally molded yellow earth into man. This man was male, named Adam. Adam then took a rib and turned it into a woman, named Eve. Adam and Eve were the ancestors of us human beings. Such words were universally accepted in past eras, and no one dared to criticize them. In China, we also have the legend of creating man from yellow earth, and the oldest emperor, Pangu, is said to have been born from within the universe like a chicken egg. We now consider these many theories of human origin to be absurd and unfounded. Why? Because Darwin's theory of evolution has replaced them.

The name of Darwin's book on the theory of evolution is "On the Origin of Species." For over a hundred years, this book has become a world-renowned masterpiece, and there are several Chinese translations of it. The essence of the theory of evolution is to overturn the idea that God created all things, and to deny the theory that all things are immutable. It says that everything evolves from simple organisms to more advanced ones. Therefore, all species are constantly changing. The ancient theory that the ancestors of various organisms have not changed from their present state is incorrect. In other words, any ancient organism may be different from the current one. The evidence is that we have discovered many strange ancient bones that have become fossils (these animals cannot be found in the current world) and many facts of biological variation. As for us humans, we naturally evolved from other animals, but we have evolved to the highest stage at present. We know that the life, habits, physiological structure, and intelligence of apes are most similar to humans, so we can conclude that humans evolved from apes, and apes evolved from other mammals. Tracing back in this way, we can trace all the way back to the simplest single-celled organisms, such as protozoa. The cell is the basic unit that constitutes living things. Small individual, single-celled organisms are small things that only have one cell, almost invisible to the human eye. Just think, to say that we humans came from this thing, isn't that a surprising theory? But don't think it's strange, this is absolutely true, because Darwin has found many pieces of evidence from the changes in plants and animals to convince you! Moreover, this kind of change takes a very long time. For example, from apes to humans, it is not known how many stages are in between, and each stage is often tens of thousands of years. If we use the changes in human affairs as a ratio, then we simply cannot see anything evolving there, because it is too slow. So why do all living things change? To put it simply, it is for the sake of adapting to the environment. Darwin's discovery on this point is indeed worthy of praise, and he has provided us with a wealth of examples as evidence. Here, we will first cite a few of the most obvious pieces of evidence for biological evolution:

The first piece is anatomical evidence. When we dissect a person or other animal, we often find useless, degenerate organs, such as the "cecum" of humans and gorillas. Not only is this thing of no use at all, but it often causes the dangerous condition of "appendicitis." If humans were created by God, why would there be such a useless organ? But if we observe things like rabbits, their cecum is very developed and also very useful. Thus, we can know that both humans and apes have gone through the stage of rabbits. When its environment changed later, and its life changed, it no longer needed the cecum, so it slowly degenerated and became its present shape. After many years, we can almost conclude that humans will no longer develop a cecum. The same principle applies to the fact that humans still retain traces of a tail. (Darwin found more than eighty such degenerated organs on the human body!)

The second piece is the fact of comparing the same species of animals. For example, insects, we all know that they should have six legs and four wings, but due to different living environments, many variations have emerged. Parasites such as lice and fleas no longer have wings because they do not need to fly at all! The hind wings of flies have also become non-existent. Also, the mouthparts of insects vary greatly in shape due to the different things they eat. Butterflies have long antennae, which grasshoppers do not have. But if you examine them closely, they are all made up of an upper lip, a lower lip, a pair of upper jaws, and a pair of lower mandibles. Also, birds all have wings, but ostriches living in the desert do not use their wings, so they are very undeveloped, while their feet walk exceptionally fast.

The third piece is the fact of embryology: Ordinary organisms are all born from eggs, and humans are also born from the union of a maternal egg and a sperm. Therefore, in the evolution of the human fetus, the evolutionary process of general organisms is revealed. It will have gills, it will have a tail, it will look like a fish for a while, and it will look like a beast for a while. This indicates that the ancestors of humans have gone through this stage.

The fourth piece is the ancient biological situation glimpsed from fossils. Because the age of the Earth's formation is very long, there have been too many changes on the surface. People who study the Earth divide the entire Earth from ancient times into four major periods: the Archean Eon, the Paleozoic Era, the Mesozoic Era, and the Cenozoic Era, and then divide each period into several epochs. In the strata of each epoch, there are fossils of the remains of organisms from that era. Now we find that the older the strata, the more fossils of simple and lower plants and animals they contain. There are very few fossils in the Archean Eon, only some lower organisms; only in the Paleozoic Era are there fish fossils, but these fish are completely different from the fish of today; in the Mesozoic Era, there were many amphibians and reptiles, such as frogs and lizards. As for bird fossils, they only appeared in the late Mesozoic Era and the early Cenozoic Era. This is truly ironclad evidence of biological evolution!

Furthermore, why do living things have to adapt to the environment? Darwin put forward two principles: natural selection and artificial selection; and the principles of "struggle for existence" and "survival of the fittest."

In terms of artificial selection, he cited many variations of organisms raised by humans as examples. The most famous is the variation of domestic pigeons: Due to human needs, there are pigeons with protruding chests, peacock tails, and fleshy balls on their eyes. This is because humans use the inherent variability of organisms to select the kind of seeds that meet their purposes and allow their offspring to reproduce. After a long time, they gradually develop into various kinds of variations. This is called artificial selection. (You can understand why the goldfish in Zhongshan Park in Beijing have so many novel appearances, right?) He intended to publish it in the society's journal. Coincidentally, the officers of the association, Lyell and Hooker, already knew that Darwin had done in-depth research on this issue, so they advised him to write a short essay with his opinions and publish it simultaneously in the July issue of the journal. In November 1859, Darwin supplemented many opinions and made a book, which is now the "On the Origin of Species" that everyone reads.

When Wallace learned that his theory was the same as Darwin's, but Darwin's research was earlier, and his arguments were rich and his thinking was profound, he was willing to give this credit to Darwin. He even called his own work "Darwinism." This kind of humility is still praised in the scientific community today, and it is many times stronger than those scholars who copy and plagiarize and pretend to be their own.

The church was very opposed to Darwin at first, but later it became silent and odorless.

Darwin gained widespread belief in England and became a first-class scientist and thinker in the world, but his research did not decline until his later years. In 1882, he died amid national mourning, and his remains were buried in Westminster Abbey, which is dedicated to burying British dignitaries.

A blood test confirmed that the root cause was eradicated.

Patient Mr. Fan Gang had suffered from gonorrhea for several years and had not been cured despite repeated treatments. Every morning, sticky and turbid fluid sealed the urethra, and the urine occasionally contained blood streaks or was turbid. The testicles were swollen, and movement was restricted and painful. Dr. Deng Yuanhe diagnosed epididymitis and prescribed "Kelinong" to eliminate gonorrhea and kill bacteria, and "Body-Strengthening Kang" was taken for endocrine treatment to eliminate testicular swelling. Reading Club

A BRIEF ACCOUNT OF THE STUDY OF CI IN THE QING DYNASTY 211

— Sizi

Ci poetry is the literature of the Song Dynasty, just like poetry in the Tang Dynasty and Qu opera in the Yuan Dynasty. Ci poetry declined greatly in the Yuan and Ming Dynasties. Although there were always people writing Ci poetry, their talents were mediocre. There were no outstanding works. Because the Yuan and Ming Dynasties were right after the Song Dynasty, and Ci poetry had already developed to its peak. As the saying goes, it is difficult to continue after extreme prosperity, so naturally they could not develop it further.

However, in the Qing Dynasty, there was a "reversal after extreme decline," and it was extremely prosperous for a time. Literary historians call it the "revival era." Mr. Liu Zigeng has the following words in his "History of Ci Poetry":

"Ci poetry is the surplus of poetry, its sprout in the Sui Dynasty, its development in the Tang Dynasty, its expansion in the Five Dynasties, its flourishing in the Northern Song Dynasty, its splendor in the Southern Song Dynasty, its pruning in the Jin Dynasty, its scattering in the Ming Dynasty, its irrigation in the early Qing Dynasty, and its harvest in the Qianlong and Jiaqing period."

This is said in the most clear and straightforward way.

Now let us give a general account of the study of Ci poetry in the Qing Dynasty.

The Ci poets in the early Qing Dynasty could not avoid the habits of the Ming Dynasty. They all followed the Tang and Five Dynasties and took the "Among the Flowers Collection" and "Grass Hut Poetry Remnants" as models. Therefore, the Ci poetry they created was lewd, vulgar, and unsightly. When Zhu Yizun rose, he changed his style, switched to the Southern Song Dynasty, and took Jiang Baishi and Zhang Yutian as the standards, forming the later trend of "the Ci poets of Zhejiang Province all learning from Baishi and Yutian," creating the so-called "Zhe School" of Ci poetry.

Speaking of the "Zhe School," we should start with Cao Jiegong. Cao Rong of Jiaxing, named Jiegong, saw that the Ci poetry of the early Qing Dynasty people followed the Ming Dynasty as the law, and he was distressed by the loss of Ci poetry. Therefore, he "worshiped elegance and rejected lewdness." Zhu Yizun strongly advocated his saying, and the Zhe School was formed. Although his Ci poetry is not entirely perfect, it is quite interesting in its emptiness. As for Zhu Yizun, his talent is extremely high, so he can create his own ideas and sweep away stale words. His "Quiet Ambition Residence Qin Fun" volume is truly the best work of enchanting Ci poetry, which ordinary hands cannot hope to match.

At the same time as Zhu, those who belonged to the Zhe School also included Li Liangnian, Shen Haozhi, Li Fu, Shen Andeng, and Gong Xianglin. Later, there were Li E, Guo Pi, Wang Ce, and Xiang Hongzu. And Li Fanshe was the "white eyebrow" of the Zhe School, most praised by the world. Xiang Hongzu was also a strong general.

In addition to the Zhe School, there were Wu Weiye and Wang Shizhen in the early Qing Dynasty, both of whom were poets and Ci poets. At the same time, several great Ci poets emerged, such as Nalan Xingde and Chen Weisong. Nalan's short verses are heartbreaking and unreadable, very much like the Southern Tang emperor Li Yu. No one in the Qing Dynasty could be compared to him. Chen Weisong was as famous as Zhu Yizun, but his style was completely different, winning with his majestic and heroic spirit. He wrote more than a hundred "Manjianghong" and "Jinlvqu" verses, and his spirit can be imagined. Also, his collection of Ci poetry is the largest in volume, with a total of thirty volumes. Almost no Ci poet in ancient and modern times can match him. In addition, Cao Zhenji, Wu Qi, Gu Zhenguan, and Peng Sunyu were also masters of the time.

Now we have to go back to the Zhe School to talk about it. The Zhe School only praised the Southern Song Dynasty, but it strived for beautiful and elegant rhymes. By the end of its run, it was all wretched work. After Qianlong and Jiaqing, the decline became even more severe. Therefore, the Zhang Huiyan and Zhang Qi brothers rose up and revived it with the Northern Song Dynasty, respecting Zhou Bangyan and suppressing Jiang Zhang, calling themselves the Changzhou School, and parted ways with the Zhe School. Their Ci poetry developed the meaning of Ci poetry in terms of profoundness and entrustment. Dong Shishi and Zhou Ji were the driving forces behind the Changzhou School. The Ci poetry of the Changzhou School dominated the entire Ci poetry scene at that time.

When the Ci poetry of the Changzhou School was popular, there was a Jiang Chunlin who did not rely on any school but only followed elegance. He was rich in talent. He lived in the era of the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom, so his Ci poetry was pure, elegant, sad, and natural. Commentators say that he was the crown of the Qing Dynasty, which is not a false statement. In addition, Zhou Ziqi, Zhuang Yu, Tan Tingxian, and others were also skilled.

In the late Qing Dynasty, Wang Pengyun, Zheng Wenzhuo, Zhu Zumou, and Kuang Zhouyi were all called strong generals. Although Wang was from Guangxi, he actually inherited the system of the Changzhou School. His theory of Ci poetry separately marked the three major tenets of "importance," "clumsiness," and "greatness." His own works can indeed adhere to this goal and strive for it. When Wenzhuo wrote Ci poetry, he adhered to the rules very strictly, but the spirit of Xiao Shu and Junyi was never concealed. Zhu's Ci poetry entered "deep sorrow and resentment" from Mengchuang, and its depression and綿渺 were impossible to detect. (Chen Sanli's words) Zhou Gu's style was biased towards the sorrowful and enchanting road, which was different from Wang and Zhu.

The Ci poetry of the Qing Dynasty for two hundred and eighty years is roughly as described above. As for the number of Ci poets, according to the Qing Ci Zong (edited by Wang Chang, up to the early Jiaqing period), the Qing Ci Zong II (edited by Wang Shaocheng, up to Daoguang), the Qing Ci Zong Continuation (edited by Huang Xianqing, up to the end of Tongzhi), and the Qing Ci Zong Supplement (edited by Ding Shaoyi, up to the end of the Qing Dynasty), the total number is three thousand. This number cannot be considered small. The number of Ci poetry collections is of course just as many. However, these Ci poetry collections are all single volumes and isolated books, and they have never been jointly published. Therefore, if we want to study Qing Ci poetry or appreciate Qing Ci poetry, we can only rely on subjective anthologies, and it is difficult to start.

Now Kaiming Bookstore has printed "Famous Ci Poetry of the Qing Dynasty," collated and edited by Mr. Chen Naiqian, which cannot but be said to be a happy event. Although only a hundred families are included, there are not many omissions of important Ci poets. The Song Dynasty Ci poetry has been compiled and published by Jigu Pavilion in front, and collated and edited by Siyinzai and Qiangcun later, which is a vast spectacle, and readers find it convenient. Now that Qing Ci poetry has been published through the efforts of Mr. Chen and Kaiming Bookstore, its merit in benefiting scholars is truly immeasurable. We hope that he can continue to print the second and third collections in the future, and make a "Complete Ci Poetry of the Qing Dynasty," then how can it be just the luck of us young people!

Author's Confession of "Literary Psychology" 212

— Zhu Guangqian

This is a book that studies literary theory. I hesitated for a while about its title. It could be called "Aesthetics," because the issues it discusses generally fall within the scope of aesthetics. Aesthetics branched out from philosophy. In the past, most aestheticians had a philosophical system in mind as a basis for deducing some aesthetic principles. This book takes a different approach. It abandons all philosophical preconceptions and studies literary creation and appreciation as psychological facts, summarizing some principles applicable to literary criticism from the facts. Its subject is literary creation and appreciation, and its perspective is largely psychological, so I do not use the name "Aesthetics," but call it "Literary Psychology." Both names have been used by people in modern times, and the difference is not very large. We can say that "Literary Psychology" is "Aesthetics" studied from a psychological point of view.

This book was written when I was a student abroad. It was originally intended to be published earlier, so Mr. Zhu Peixian's preface was written in London in 1932. Later, I felt that some places still needed to be revised, so it was put aside for four years. During these four years, I used it as a lecture note at Tsinghua University for a year, and this year I selectively lectured on it in the "Poetry Theory" course at Peking University. Every time I lectured, I revised the original manuscript once. In terms of quantity alone, the manuscript now being printed exceeds the original manuscript that I asked Mr. Zhu Peixian to review four years ago by one-third. Chapters six, seven, eight, ten, and eleven are all newly added.

In these newly added five chapters, my views on aesthetics have undergone a very important change compared with when I wrote the first draft four years ago. In the past, I was bound by the formalist aesthetics passed down from Kant to Croce. I thought that aesthetic experience was purely a formal intuition. In concentration, we appreciate an isolated image without any other distractions, so abstract thinking, association, moral concepts, etc. are all outside the scope of aesthetic perception. Now, I realize that life is an organism; scientific, ethical, and aesthetic activities can be distinguished in theory, but they cannot be separated in fact, making each other isolated. Therefore, I fundamentally oppose the mechanical view on which Croce's formalist aesthetics is based, and the abstract analytical method used. I have made this change of attitude very clear in Chapter 11 – "A Critique of Croce's Aesthetics." I revised the first draft twice, both times correcting the arguments I had previously made following the formalist school from this skeptical attitude towards formalism. I dare not say that I have overthrown formalist aesthetics. Many of the principles it affirms are indelible. Its problem is that it is too biased. My contribution to it is only a "patching up of loopholes." Holding prejudices is the most misleading thing in academic research. Intentionally trying to reconcile and compromise, and intentionally being biased, are both holding prejudices. I originally had no intention of reconciling and compromising, but I finally went down the road of compromise. This may be the result of my being too cautious and not daring to easily believe in one-sided theories and one-sided facts.

Now, people in general seem to still have an inappropriate contempt for the study of literary theory. Creators say, "I can create without your literary theories; you still can't create even with those literary theories." Appreciators say, "The beauty and mystery of literature and art cannot be analyzed by scientific methods. If you analyze it by scientific methods, the result is to 'break the seven-jeweled building into pieces.'" These words are indeed "well-founded and reasonable," but those who study literary theory do not necessarily have to eliminate their right to exist because of this. He can defend himself as follows:

Everything has research value. Science does not divide worldly things into two types: "should be studied" and "should not be studied." Unless you are deliberately ignorant, unless you force others to follow you in being deliberately ignorant, literary creators and appreciators have no reason to despise others for engaging in scientific activities in literature and art, that is, seeking principles about literature and art based on the facts of creation and appreciation.

There are only two reasons why a person studies a subject: one is that the subject has direct practical use for him, like child psychology for educators; the other is that although it has no direct practical use, its problems easily arouse curiosity, and people want to study it, just like children want to drill into a maze to find a way out, simply because the matter itself is interesting. Regarding the study of literary theory, even if we step back and admit that it has no practical use for creation and appreciation, we cannot just write it off. Since it has problems, it can stimulate curiosity and arouse research interest.

Moreover, is the study of literary theory not useful for creation and appreciation at all? First, in terms of creation, while it is true that those with "high eyes" may have "low hands," it seems that there are not many with "low eyes" and "high hands." Literature and art in modern times have largely departed from "natural expression" and entered the stage of "intentional depiction," that is, it has become a "self-conscious" activity. Every artist sooner or later will have to think about content and form, art and life, freehand and realism, and other issues. What he personally experiences in practice, such as Leonardo da Vinci's "Treatise on Painting," Goethe and Eckermann's "Conversations," Rodin's "Art," and Flaubert's "Letters," are certainly very valuable, but every artist does not necessarily have the time and interest, especially not necessarily the calm analytical ability, to build a theory. If he pays a little attention to the results obtained by those who study literary theory, he may not hold biased, or even wrong, views on the problems he usually thinks about himself. In literature and art, the bad effects of wrong views are no less than those of inferior skills.

Speaking of appreciation, the study of literary theory is simply indispensable. Since it is called appreciation, one must understand the criteria of "value" and the essence of art. If you have not decided what is beautiful, you have no reason to say that this painting is more beautiful than that painting; if you do not understand the essence of art, you have no reason to say that this work is art and that work is not art. There are indeed many people in the world who criticize literature and art without studying aesthetics, but they are like sailors talking about astronomy and nurses talking about medicine, relying entirely on crude experience without a rigorous and systematic theory as a basis. I dare not ignore crude experience, but I dare say that it is not enough, and sometimes it is misleading.

Taking this opportunity, I may as well briefly talk about my personal experience. I never dreamed that one day I would go down the road of aesthetics. I have been a student at several universities for fourteen years, studying many irrelevant subjects, dissecting sharks, making stained sections, reading architectural history, learning symbolic nomenclature, and using smoked drums and electrical reaction tables to test psychological reactions, but I have never taken an aesthetics class. My original center of interest was first literature, then psychology, and third philosophy. Because I liked literature, I was forced to study the standards of criticism, art and life, art and nature, content and form, language and thought; because I liked psychology, I was forced to study the relationship between imagination and emotion, the psychological activities of creation and appreciation, and the individual differences in taste; because I liked philosophy, I was forced to study the works of Kant, Hegel, and Croce on aesthetics. In this way, aesthetics has become the connecting thread of the several subjects I like. I now believe that it is a great lack if people who study literature, art, psychology, and philosophy ignore aesthetics.

The book includes three articles on "Modern Experimental Aesthetics," which briefly describe the paths taken by modern psychologists in doing aesthetic experiments, the methods used, and the results obtained. These are all dry facts, but I believe that the most important training for scientists is to learn to value dry facts and find interest in dry facts, so these three articles may be helpful to literary psychologists.

This book generally discusses literature and art. I have written another book, "Poetics," which applies the basic principles of this book to discuss the problems of poetry. At the same time, it conducts a theoretical study of Chinese poetry.

The completion of this book relies on the help of many friends. The first is Mr. Zhu Peixian. He carefully reviewed the original manuscript for me in his hurried journey in Europe, wrote a preface, and gave me many careful criticisms. Chapter 6, "Aesthetic Feeling and Association," was revised because he was not satisfied with the original manuscript. The second is Mr. Xia Gaizun. He allowed this relatively specialized book to have the opportunity to be published in this year of book industry depression. Finally, it is my wife, Jin Wu. She gave me much encouragement when this book was drafted, and then painstakingly corrected the mistakes again and again after the manuscript was completed. Taking this opportunity, I would like to express my gratitude to them.

"A Story of Human History" 213

— Qingshui

We know very well that children like to read books about past lives and stories. Because history separates people for too long, the imagination, wisdom, skills, and tools used by people before were all hundreds or thousands of times clumsier than those of today. Therefore, their process of surviving and struggling was so strange and bizarre. When we see it, we not only feel some horror, but also laugh so hard that our stomachs hurt, and exclaim "Stupid people, stupid people!" However, this is an unavoidable mistake caused by the various environments of our ancestors' limitations in era, knowledge, and tools, and it is not that their wisdom is not as good as ours. In this historical process, we really need to deeply understand and strive for. Not only do we need to know what is so, but also what must be so.

This subject, this kind of , also existed in the past, but some said it was too bizarre, and completely mythologized it, which made children feel insufficient. Some were written too plainly, describing it realistically, preaching with a straight face, obscure and difficult to understand, simply unable to be read, and falling asleep after listening. Therefore, the impression that this subject and this knowledge have on the minds of any of our children is so vague that as soon as they leave the school gate, they forget it cleanly and completely return it to the teacher.

This book, "A Story of Human History" (The Child’s Story of the Human Race) by Ramon Koffman, is a rare good book. It is very suitable for adults to read, and it goes without saying that it is most beneficial for children to read. "Insect Stories" is a good book, but its content is limited to a certain aspect. "The Wind in the Willows" is a good book, but its material is not so extensive. Even "The Story of Mankind" by Van Loon, which everyone knows and reads, has less and fresher material than this book. This book uses artistic means and simple and clear language to write a very interesting book that is easy to read and enjoyable to read about the ancient life history of mankind. It is neither a fictitious myth, which makes readers unconsciously pursue the paradise of illusory poetry; nor is it a flat and straightforward account book writing, like a dead snake, but rather an undulating and winding method of peeling bananas and drawing silk, analyzing it layer by layer, clarifying the progress of the history of ancient human life, so that readers can satisfactorily understand the important question of "why is it so" that they cannot understand. This is true history, history that meets scientific requirements, which is most sufficient for us to understand the past and present state and process of people, as well as all the interconnected historical relationships. Divided into sections and paragraphs, arranged in an orderly manner, like flowing water connected into one, equally simple, equally clear, equally tortuous and beautiful narrative, like a myth story that is easy to recite and read, it is truly appropriate to say that it is a rare book.

When "Children's Day" came, I wrote articles for several newspapers, all talking about such a question. I said, "More fairy tale books that explain the meaning of human history and natural phenomena should be compiled, printed, or translated with beautiful words for our children to read." "This year, children's literature is almost dying. If we cannot create good fairy tales for children to read, then translating some excellent works for children to read, such as the ones that Benkakko gives to children of the 20th century, is also a work of great merit." (Mr. Zhou Zuoren seems to have said something like this) The editor spent three years to compile this good book that is sufficient to satisfy children's intellectual desires; the Japanese scholar Torii Ryuzo praised it as "not only can it be used as a children's book; it is also very valuable as a general reading material" (translator's preface). This statement is the most fair. The advertisement for "The Wind in the Willows" says, "This is a book for young people, so it may be exclusively for young people, as well as people who still have a young spirit alive in their hearts. This is life, sunlight, flowing water, trees, dusty roads, and the warmth of the fireside in winter. It is comparable to 'Alice's Adventures in Wonderland' and becomes a classic." After reading this book, I admired the book's light, beautiful, and witty writing—especially the first two or three chapters are beautifully written, unprecedented—and thought that it would be fitting and appropriate to move this passage to give to each other as a gift.

The author's original preface says: "I wrote this book happily. If you read it and get the same happiness, it is my fortune." Dear young people! Please accept the words of "your good friend" and read in one breath such a good book he wrote for you that is full of life and content and can be used as spiritual food!
